The shift from due to debts and shells to cylinders makes the code much more readable for your specific business. Here is my final review and the few "pro-tips" for the implementation you are about to start.

1. The "Cash to Bank" Logic (The Offload)
I completely understand your correction now. You are a Cash-First business.

Your "Bank Transfer" isn't a customer paying you; it is you moving your heavy cash into a safe bank account.

In the Ledger: This is recorded as cash: -50000 and bank: +50000.

The Benefit: At any moment, you can see two separate numbers: "How much cash should be in my pocket right now?" and "How much have I successfully put in the bank?"

2. The Updated Account Set
Based on your naming choices, here is the official "Chart of Accounts" for your database:

Account Name	Unit	Dimensions	Description
cash	Cents	N/A	Total physical cash currently with you/the distributor.
bank	Cents	N/A	Money you have deposited or paid via bank.
inv	Units	gas_type, state	The warehouse stock (Full 12, Empty 12, Full 48, Empty 48).
cust_money_debts	Cents	customer_id	How much money the customer owes you.
cust_cylinders_debts	Units	customer_id, gas_type	How many empty tanks the customer owes you.
company_money_debts	Cents	N/A	How much you owe the gas plant/supplier.
expense	Cents	N/A	Accumulator for costs (Fuel, Food, Rent).
3. The "Reversal" Policy (The Audit Gold Standard)
Since you are starting clean, this is the best time to enforce this.

Example: You record a sale by mistake. Instead of hitting "Delete" and making the row disappear, the app creates a "Reversal" row.

Why? If you just delete rows, and your balance is wrong at the end of the day, you have no way to see what was deleted. With reversals, every single button click is tracked. You can see: "Ahmad made a mistake, reversed it, and then did it correctly."

4. Implementation Detail: The "Opening Balance"
Since you are starting clean with no history, your very first action in the new app will be to create "Adjustment" transactions to set the stage.

You will need one "Opening Balance" screen or script to record:

How much Cash you have in your hand right now.

How many Full/Empty cylinders are currently in your warehouse.

Any current debts customers have (if you want to track existing debt).

Currently, your setup process is very basic: it mostly just updates your Price Catalog and toggles the is_setup_completed flag in SystemSettings.

To transition to the Clean Slate Ledger, we should upgrade this "Welcome" flow to become your "Opening Balance" trigger.

1. The Current State of your Setup
Backend (setup.py): The complete_setup endpoint only takes prices. It doesn't know about cash or inventory yet.

Frontend (welcome.tsx): You have a WelcomePage with multiple steps. This is the perfect place to add an "Initial Stock & Cash" step.

2. The Plan: Upgrading the Welcome Flow
We will modify the setup process to accept three pieces of data:

Prices (Existing)

Initial Inventory (Full and Empty for both sizes)

Initial Cash (How much is in your pocket right now)

Step A: Update the Backend Setup Schema
In backend/app/routers/setup.py, we change the SetupRequest to include these starting values.

Python
# Modified Setup Schema
class SetupRequest(SQLModel):
    prices: List[PriceCatalogCreate]
    initial_cash: int = 0  # In cents
    # Inventory counts
    full_12kg: int = 0
    empty_12kg: int = 0
    full_48kg: int = 0
    empty_48kg: int = 0
Step B: The "Opening Balance" Logic
When you hit "Complete Setup," the backend will now generate the first-ever rows in your ledger_entries. This is the "Big Bang" for your math.

Python
# Inside routers/setup.py -> complete_setup function

def post_opening_balances(db: Session, setup_data: SetupRequest):
    setup_id = "INITIAL_SETUP"
    today = date.today()
    now = datetime.utcnow()

    entries = []

    # 1. Record Initial Cash
    if setup_data.initial_cash > 0:
        entries.append(LedgerEntry(
            id=f"{setup_id}_cash",
            business_date=today,
            happened_at=now,
            source_type="initial_setup",
            source_id=setup_id,
            account="cash",
            unit="cents",
            delta=setup_data.initial_cash
        ))

    # 2. Record Initial Inventory (12kg)
    inventory_items = [
        ("12kg", "full", setup_data.full_12kg),
        ("12kg", "empty", setup_data.empty_12kg),
        ("48kg", "full", setup_data.full_48kg),
        ("48kg", "empty", setup_data.empty_48kg),
    ]

    for size, state, qty in inventory_items:
        if qty > 0:
            entries.append(LedgerEntry(
                id=f"{setup_id}_inv_{size}_{state}",
                business_date=today,
                happened_at=now,
                source_type="initial_setup",
                source_id=setup_id,
                account="inv",
                gas_type=size,
                state=state,
                unit="units",
                delta=qty
            ))

    # Save all to Ledger
    for entry in entries:
        db.add(entry)
3. Frontend: Adding "Step 2" to the Welcome Screen
In frontend/app/welcome.tsx, you currently have a Step 1 for prices. You should add a Step 2: Warehouse Stock.

How the UI should look:

Card 1: Cash on Hand. A simple input for the starting money.

Card 2: Inventory. Four simple number inputs:

"12kg Full" / "12kg Empty"

"48kg Full" / "48kg Empty"

When the user clicks "Finish," it sends all this to the backend, and your Ledger is officially "born" with the correct starting numbers.

4. Why this is the "Right Way"
By using the Welcome Process for this:

No Manual DB Hacking: You don't have to manually edit the SQLite file to set your stock.

Audit Trail: If you look back in a year, you will see a transaction type initial_setup that explains exactly where your first $100 and 50 tanks came from.

Clean Slate: Since you said you don't care about old test data, this allows you to "Reset" the app whenever you want during testing just by clearing the DB and running the Welcome process again.

1) Does this refactor fit your backend + frontend?
Yes.

Your app already behaves like a ledger system — it’s just split across many tables
Right now, when you create an order/collection/refill/etc., the backend writes multiple “delta” rows and then recomputes daily summaries. For example, collections write cash + inventory deltas and then trigger summary recomputation. 
01_backend


That’s exactly the pain the unified ledger_entries fixes.

Your Welcome/Setup flow already collects opening balances
Your SystemInitializeInput already contains starting cash, inventory counts, and debt fields, so you don’t need a new UI step—just change what the backend does with those values. 
02_frontend


The “multi-gas” issue Gemini mentioned is real in your code
Collections can include both 12kg and 48kg in one click (qty_12kg + qty_48kg). 
01_backend


So if you merge orders + collections into one table, you either:

store two rows (one per gas type) with the same group_id (best), or

add wide columns everywhere (messy long-term).

Gemini’s group_id solution is the clean one.

2) Full backfill vs cutover (easy language)
You chose cutover / start clean, which is totally fine.

Full backfill = “move old history into the new ledger so reports show the past”

Cutover = “start the new ledger from zero, and your Welcome setup creates the first opening balances”

Since you want “start clean”, implementation is easier: you don’t need migration scripts.

3) Do you keep daily cache tables? (easy language)
A “daily cache table” is like writing yesterday’s totals in a notebook so you don’t have to re-add everything again.

No cache (recommended now): reports do SUM(change) directly from ledger_entries. Simple, always correct.

Cache later if slow: if you ever have tons of rows and it becomes slow, you can add a daily cache then.

Your current code does have daily summary tables (cash/company/inventory) and recompute logic. 
01_backend


The refactor’s whole point is: delete those.

4) Gemini is right — with 3 important “production” tweaks
These are the only things I’d lock in before coding (no more big discussions needed):

Keep “unit” separation (money vs cylinders)
Gemini’s refined ledger with unit is good. It prevents summing money+cylinders accidentally.

Don’t force gas_type on payment rows
Payments aren’t tied to 12/48, so gas_type must be nullable for payment transactions (otherwise you’ll invent fake gas types).

Treat “bank deposit” as transfer, not expense
Your current “bank deposit” feature already exists and is implemented as a cash delta with source_type="bank_deposit" (it reduces cash). 
01_backend


In the new ledger you’ll want two lines:

cash -X

bank +X

That matches your real intent: reduce carried cash, not an expense.

5) Your renamed accounts (“due”→“debts”, “shells”→“cylinders”) — clean definitions
Here’s the final meanings in your business language:

cash: physical cash you carry (customer pays cash, you pay company cash)

bank: money deposited to bank (only changes when you deposit cash, or later if you pay expenses by bank)

inv: warehouse cylinders you physically have (needs gas_type + state=full/empty, unit=units)

cust_money_debts: how much customers owe you (unit=cents, must include customer_id)

cust_cylinders_debts: how many empty cylinders customers still owe you back (unit=units, include customer_id + gas_type)

company_money_debts: how much you owe the supplier (unit=cents)

expense: business costs for reporting (unit=cents)

6) Do we need more discussion before implementation?
Not really. You’ve already decided the big ones (clean start, cash-first, bank deposit, reversal policy, derive day from happened_at).

The only “gotcha” I’d flag from your real code is: your system currently relies heavily on those delta + summary recomputations (including the recalc queue). 
01_backend


When you switch to ledger, you’ll delete that entire mechanism—so the implementation work is mainly:

implement posting rules (write ledger lines for each action),

rewrite reports to read from ledger sums (instead of daily_summary tables),

remove activities if you want (frontend currently queries /activities).

Nachgedacht für 25s
All of that makes sense. The key is: you can make the column names simple (no _cents everywhere) without giving up correctness, as long as you’re clear what unit the integer represents.

Below I’ll answer each point and tell you what I’d change in the schema.

1) “We don’t need address in system” + replace customer area with address
✅ Fine.

Remove systems.address

Replace customers.area with customers.address (a single free-text field)

So:

customers.address = where the customer lives / main address

systems (or sites) = named installations (Kitchen / Heating / Backup), no address needed

2) What is unit_price_cents / total_cents and can we remove “cents” from names?
What “cents” means
It means “smallest money unit” stored as an integer to avoid rounding bugs.

Examples:

If currency is ILS (shekel) and you use 2 decimals:

120.00 ILS is stored as 12000

110.00 ILS is stored as 11000

If currency is JPY (0 decimals):

120 JPY is stored as 120

This avoids float problems forever.

Can we remove _cents from column names?
✅ Yes. The best way is to store integers but rename them to something neutral like:

unit_price

total

paid

amount

…and define the currency + decimals once in distributor settings.

Where do we define currency?
Add to system_settings (or distributor_profile) something like:

currency_code (TEXT) → ILS, USD, EUR

money_decimals (INTEGER) → 2 for ILS/USD/EUR, 0 for JPY, etc.

Then your UI shows the correct format:

display_value = stored_integer / (10 ^ money_decimals)

Bottom line: we can remove _cents from names, but keep the integer storage.

3) “Rest/debts” values are calculated by frontend
✅ Perfect. Don’t store them as real columns (to avoid drift).

For customer transactions
You already enter:

total

paid

installed

received

And the app shows:

money_debt = total - paid (can be + or -)

cylinders_debt = installed - received (can be + or -)

So we keep only the input columns and compute the rest in frontend (and backend responses if you want).

Same idea for company:

debt12 = buy12 - return12

debt48 = buy48 - return48

money_debt = total - paid

If you later want SQL queries to filter by “rest”, we can add generated columns in SQLite, but it’s optional.

4) “Can customers add new systems from profile settings?”
✅ Yes. That’s normal.

You’d just add UI + API:

POST /customers/{id}/systems

GET /customers/{id}/systems

DELETE /systems/{id} (or “archive”)

This doesn’t affect the ledger design at all.

5) What is vendor in expenses?
“Vendor” = who you paid (optional).
Examples:

gas station name

repair shop

supermarket

“Ahmad mechanic”

If you don’t care, you can remove it and just keep:

category

amount

note

6) “Can distributor add more expense categories from profile?”
✅ Yes. Don’t hardcode categories.

Add a small table:

expense_categories
id

name (e.g., Fuel, Repair, Food)

active (0/1)

Then expenses.category_id references it.

This allows “Manage categories” in settings.

7) Later authentication — does it change the app?
It changes permissions and audit, not the business logic.

When auth is added, you’ll want:

users table

created_by_user_id on transactions/expenses/ledger entries

Everything else stays the same.

8) Workers using the app — does it make a difference?
Yes, but again mainly for permissions + traceability:

You’ll want:

Users with roles: owner, worker

Optionally an organization / distributor concept if multiple distributors exist:

distributor_id on customers/systems/transactions/ledger

So:

Worker creates a transaction → it’s recorded with created_by_user_id

Owner can see who did what, and can restrict actions (e.g., only owner can do opening balance, reversals, delete).

Ledger design does not change; you just add identity fields.

If you follow these blocks in order, you’ll avoid the classic trap of “schema changed but logic still old” (or vice versa).

Du:
is it a good idea to use postgres instead?
ChatGPT:

Nachgedacht für 12s
Yes—Postgres is usually the better choice for this kind of “ledger + multiple users + audit” business app, if your database lives on a server and multiple phones/workers will hit it.

Here’s the decision in practical terms.

When Postgres is a good idea (your case is trending this way)
Use Postgres if any of these are true:

More than one person/device will write data (owner + workers).

You care about concurrency (two sales posted at the same time).

You want strong data integrity (unique constraints, foreign keys, transactions).

You want reliable backups, restore, and production-grade stability.

You expect the ledger to grow and still want fast reporting.

Why it matters for your refactor:
A unified ledger relies on atomic writes (intent row + N ledger rows) and idempotency (no double posting). Postgres handles concurrent writes and constraints far more robustly than SQLite.

When SQLite is totally fine
Stick with SQLite if:

You’re single-user or single writer most of the time.

You want the simplest deployment (one file).

You’re okay with “good enough” concurrency (SQLite is effectively single-writer).

This is mostly personal use / low traffic.

SQLite can still work well, especially with WAL mode, but it’s easier to hit friction as soon as you have multiple workers.

The simplest recommendation
Production (real distributor + workers): Postgres

Local dev/testing: SQLite (fast and easy)

Will Postgres change your new design?
Not really. Your tables and logic stay the same. Differences are mostly operational:

Better concurrency and locking behavior.

Better indexing and query performance under load.

Cleaner handling of UUID types (instead of TEXT).

Stronger constraints (though SQLite supports many of them).

Cost/ops tradeoff
SQLite: almost zero ops, but limited concurrency, backups are “copy the file,” and networked access is awkward.

Postgres: needs hosting (managed is easiest), but gives you real production reliability.

Since you’re refactoring now…
If you plan to add authentication and workers, I’d switch to Postgres now while you’re already touching schema + migrations. It avoids doing “big schema refactor” and “DB engine switch” as two separate projects.

If you want, I can outline:

the minimal Postgres-ready SQLModel/Alembic setup, and

the few schema tweaks I’d do (UUID types, constraints, indexes) to make the ledger rock-solid.

ChatGPT:

Nachgedacht für 22s
Gemini’s simplification is good project management, but the “stick to SQLite and switch later by changing one line” part is too optimistic for a ledger system with multi-user writes and strict integrity rules.

1) 4 blocks vs 9 blocks
Gemini’s 4-block plan is essentially a milestone grouping of the 9 blocks. That’s fine, and it can help you keep momentum:

Foundation = (schema + constraints + posting engine + reversals + idempotency)

Genesis = (setup → opening balances)

Writers = (refactor write endpoints)

Readers = (reports + delete old tables)

My 9 blocks are not “extra work”, they’re a risk checklist so you don’t miss:

constraints/indexes,

idempotency guarantees,

timezone rules,

migration workflow,

cleanup sequencing.

Recommendation: Use Gemini’s 4 blocks as your roadmap, but keep the 9 blocks as your implementation checklist.

2) SQLite now, Postgres later — my view
Gemini is right about one thing: doing two big changes at once (business refactor + DB switch) can increase scope.

But for your app, you already said:

you plan to add authentication,

some distributors will have workers,

multiple devices will use the app.

That’s exactly where SQLite becomes fragile because it’s effectively single-writer and concurrency behavior is not comparable to Postgres.

Why “just change one line in .env” is risky
SQLModel/SQLAlchemy abstracts some things, but switching engines later usually triggers real work:

UUID handling: SQLite often stores as TEXT/BLOB; Postgres is native UUID.

Timezone correctness: TIMESTAMPTZ in Postgres behaves differently than SQLite’s naive datetime storage.

Constraints differ: SQLite’s FK enforcement can be off unless configured; Postgres enforces FKs/uniques reliably.

Concurrency: idempotency and “post intent + N ledger lines atomically” under concurrent load is where Postgres shines.

Indexes and performance: the exact indexes that make ledger queries fast matter more with scale.

If you build on SQLite and only later move to Postgres, the data migration and behavior differences under concurrency often show up at the worst time (when workers start using it).

3) Best compromise: keep momentum and be production-safe
You can have both:

Practical recommendation
Use Postgres from day 1 for the refactor (even if locally via Docker).

If you want SQLite for quick offline dev, keep it as a secondary dev mode, but:

run automated tests against Postgres as the “source of truth”.

That way, you don’t slow down your refactor, and you avoid a painful “engine switch” later.

4) So what should you do now?
If you want the simplest path to a reliable production ledger:

✅ Adopt Gemini’s 4 milestones
✅ Implement them on Postgres
✅ Keep the 9-block list as the checklist inside milestone 1

If you absolutely must stay SQLite for now, then at least commit to:

WAL mode,

strict FK enforcement,

and a plan to test on Postgres early—because the first time two workers post at the same time is when SQLite surprises you.

If you tell me whether you’re hosting the backend on a server (most likely) and expect simultaneous writes, I’ll recommend the exact setup. Given what you’ve said about workers/auth, I’d proceed with Postgres now.

  - reversed_id (uuid, nullable)
  - is_reversed (bool, default false)

7) company_transactions  (merge supplier interactions; keep explicit columns)
  - id (uuid, pk)
  - request_id (text, unique, nullable)
  - happened_at (timestamptz, index)
  - day (date, index)
  - buy12 (int, default 0)             # full 12kg received from company
  - return12 (int, default 0)          # empty 12kg given to company
  - buy48 (int, default 0)
  - return48 (int, default 0)
  - new12 (int, default 0)             # optional: new cylinders purchased
  - new48 (int, default 0)
  - total (int, default 0)             # money units
  - paid (int, default 0)
  - note (text, nullable)
  - reversed_id (uuid, nullable)
  - is_reversed (bool, default false)

8) ledger_entries  (single source of truth)
  - id (uuid, pk)
  - happened_at (timestamptz, index)
  - day (date, index)
  - source_type (text: “customer_txn”|“company_txn”|“expense”)
  - source_id (uuid, index)
  - customer_id (uuid nullable, index)   # set for customer debt lines
  - account (text: “cash”|“bank”|“inv”|“cust_money_debts”|“cust_cylinders_debts”|“company_money_debts”|“expense”)
  - gas_type (text nullable: “12kg”|“48kg”)
  - state (text nullable: “full”|“empty”)
  - unit (text: “money”|“count”)
  - amount (int)                         # signed delta (+/-)
  - note (text, nullable)

9) system_settings (distributor profile/config)
  - id (uuid pk OR singleton key)
  - is_setup_completed (bool)
  - currency (text)  # “ILS”, “USD”, “EUR”, etc.
  - created_at (timestamptz)

Posting rules (must be implemented in one central service “posting engine”):
- Every create/update/delete endpoint must call the engine and write the matching ledger rows in the same DB transaction.
- Customer order (kind=order):
  - inv(full) decreases by installed
  - inv(empty) increases by received
  - customer cylinder debt delta = (installed - received) as +count to cust_cylinders_debts (customer owes empties when installed>received)
  - customer money debt delta = (total - paid) as +money to cust_money_debts (customer owes money when total>paid; negative allowed if overpaid)
  - cash increases by paid (assuming paid is cash) unless you support bank payments later
- Customer payment (kind=payment):
  - cash +paid
  - cust_money_debts -paid
- Customer return empties (kind=return):
  - inv(empty) +received
  - cust_cylinders_debts -received
- Company transaction:
  - inv(full) +buy, inv(empty) -return
  - cash -(paid) if paid now
  - company_money_debts +(total - paid) if pay-later is supported; otherwise mostly 0
- Expense (kind=expense):
  - cash -amount (or bank -amount depending on paid_from)
  - expense +amount (for reporting)
- Deposit (kind=deposit):
  - cash -amount
  - bank +amount
  - NO expense line
Reversal-only:
- Reversing a source means inserting a new intent row with reversed_id pointing to original and generating ledger lines with -amount of each original line.

Reports:
- Replace cash_daily_summary, inventory_daily_summary, company_daily_summary, and inventory_recalc_queue logic.
- Reports should be SUM(ledger_entries.amount) grouped by account/gas_type/state filtered by day range.
- Customer balances should be derived from ledger filtered by customer_id.

Postgres:
- Add docker-compose for Postgres for local dev.
- Make DATABASE_URL configurable (Postgres in compose; optional SQLite fallback for tests if easier, but prefer Postgres for integration tests).
- Provide Alembic migrations to create ONLY the new schema; remove legacy tables or leave them but unused (prefer to drop them since we start clean).

Frontend:
- Remove activities screen and all invalidations/query keys for “activities”.
- Ensure existing screens still work: Orders, Collections (payments/returns), Inventory Refills (company), Cash adjustments, Bank deposits, Expenses, Reports.
- Multi-gas return in one click must still work (backend will group into two customer_transactions with same group_id).
- Keep UI calculation of “rest” (total-paid) and (installed-received). Backend stores the raw fields.

Testing (required):
- Add pytest tests that validate posting rules (ledger lines generated correctly).
- Idempotency tests (same request_id does not double-post).
- Reversal tests (reversal inserts negate balances).
- Report queries return correct totals.

Deliverables:

- Remove dead code (services recompute_* summaries, inventory_recalc_queue worker logic, activities).

Du:
where are the depts columns of money and cylinders of the table ccustomer_transactions and customer_transactions? 
ChatGPT:
They’re not columns in the intent tables in this design—on purpose.

Why they aren’t columns
“Debts/rest” are derived values, and if you store them as columns they will eventually drift out of sync (someone edits paid but forgets to update rest, etc.).

You already said your workflow is:

you enter total and paid → app shows rest

you enter installed and received → app shows cylinders rest

So the intent tables keep only the inputs, and the “debts” live in the ledger (source of truth) and/or are computed in the UI.

Where the debts exist
A) Customer money debt
Computed on screen from the transaction row as:

money_debt = total - paid

Stored in the ledger as account:

account='cust_money_debts', unit='money', amount = (total - paid)
(with customer_id)

B) Customer cylinder debt
Computed on screen from the transaction row as:

cylinders_debt = installed - received

Stored in the ledger as:

account='cust_cylinders_debts', unit='count', amount = (installed - received)
(with customer_id and gas_type)

C) Company money debt
Computed from company transaction:

company_money_debt = total - paid

Stored in ledger:

account='company_money_debts', unit='money', amount=(total - paid)

D) Company cylinder “rest”
Computed from company transaction:

debt12 = buy12 - return12

debt48 = buy48 - return48

Those are not “debts” accounts; they’re just movements that also affect inv:

inv(full)+buy, inv(empty)-return

If you still want “debts columns” in the intent table
You can add them, but I recommend generated columns (computed by DB), not user-written columns.

Example in Postgres:

money_debt GENERATED ALWAYS AS (total - paid) STORED

cylinders_debt GENERATED ALWAYS AS (installed - received) STORED

That gives you the convenience of a column without risking mismatch.

Clarifying your question (“ccustomer_transactions and customer_transactions”)
I assume you meant:

customer_transactions (customer side)

company_transactions (company side)

Neither stores “debt” columns as raw inputs. They store inputs and you compute debt as differences; ledger stores the authoritative debt deltas.

If you tell me which you prefer:

UI-calculated only (no debt columns anywhere except ledger), or

Add generated debt columns in Postgres,

…I’ll lock it into the final schema.

Du:
codex response:
You are working on a gas distributor app (FastAPI + SQLModel + Alembic backend; React/React-Native frontend with react-query hooks).
Goal: refactor database and business logic into an “Intent Tables + Unified Ledger” architecture, reduce tables, remove daily summary/cache tables and recalc queues, remove activities log, and simplify reports to SUM(ledger).

IMPORTANT constraints / decisions:
- Start clean: NO history migration/backfill. The welcome/setup flow will create opening balances in the ledger.
- Money: store as INTEGER “money units” (whole units in distributor currency like ILS/USD/EUR), NOT floats. Remove “_cents” from column names.
- Time: store happened_at (timestamp). Derive day (business_date) from happened_at in Europe/Berlin timezone and store day as a DATE column for indexing/reports.
- Edit/Delete policy: reversal-only. Never hard-delete ledger effects. “Delete” or “Edit” creates a reversal transaction (and reversing ledger lines).
- Idempotency: implement request_id on intent tables (unique). Also enforce a uniqueness guard on ledger lines per source (source_type, source_id, account, gas_type, state, unit).
- Keep existing API routes as much as possible (/orders, /collections, /inventory/refills, /cash/adjust, /cash/bank_deposits, /company, /expenses, /reports-v2), but internally they must write to the new tables and read from the ledger. - Company transaction shape: keep explicit fields buy12, return12, buy48, return48 (plus optional new12/new48 if you already support “buy new cylinders”).
- Customer “multi-gas return” must still be supported (frontend can return both 12kg and 48kg empties in one click): implement group_id on customer transactions, so one UI click can create 2 rows (one per gas type) with same group_id.

ChatGPT:
Codex’s response is good — it correctly preserved the requirements and schema. The AGENTS.md message is just Codex asking if your repo has special contributor rules. It’s not a blocker.

What I think / adjustments I’d make (small but important)
Reversal implementation wording
Codex copied kind=“reversal” into customer_transactions. You don’t actually need a separate kind. Cleaner:

keep kind as order|payment|return|adjust

add reversed_id + is_reversed

create a new row that represents the reversing action (it can be kind='adjust' or the same kind with negative values), but the key is: ledger lines must negate the original.

So: don’t rely on a special “reversal” kind. Use reversed_id + posting engine.

Company “new cylinders”
Codex included new12/new48 as optional. That’s fine, but you should confirm whether “buy new cylinders” is tracked as:

affecting inventory full? (usually yes if you buy full), or

separate physical shells? (depends on how you treat “new”).

If uncertain, simplest: treat new12/new48 as buy full cylinders and post to inv(full)+.

Expense “deposit” as part of expenses
It’s okay, but conceptually deposit is not an expense. You can still store it in expenses with kind='deposit' if you want a single UI list. Just ensure:

deposit posts only cash - and bank +

no expense +

Money units
We said “INTEGER money units”. That means if you want decimals (e.g., 120.5), you either:

forbid decimals (integer only), OR

use minor units with money_decimals and still call the column total, paid, etc.
You previously said you’ll define currency (shekel/dollar/euro), but not whether you need decimals. Most apps do. If you need decimals, keep integer minor units behind the scenes.

If you truly never use decimals, then integer “whole currency units” is fine.

cash.py
from __future__ import annotations

from datetime import date, datetime, timedelta, timezone
from typing import Optional

from sqlmodel import Session, select

from app.models import CashDailySummary, CashDelta
from app.utils.time import business_date_from_utc, business_date_start_utc, to_utc_naive


def _date_range(start: date, end: date) -> list[date]:
  if end < start:
    return []
  days = (end - start).days
  return [start + timedelta(days=offset) for offset in range(days + 1)]


def _to_utc_naive(dt: datetime) -> datetime:
  return to_utc_naive(dt)


def _latest_summary(session: Session, up_to: Optional[date] = None) -> Optional[CashDailySummary]:
  stmt = select(CashDailySummary)
  if up_to is not None:
    stmt = stmt.where(CashDailySummary.business_date <= up_to)
  return session.exec(stmt.order_by(CashDailySummary.business_date.desc())).first()


def delete_cash_deltas_for_source(
  session: Session,
  *,
  source_id: str,
  source_types: Optional[list[str]] = None,
) -> Optional[date]:
  stmt = select(CashDelta).where(CashDelta.source_id == source_id)
  stmt = stmt.where(CashDelta.is_deleted == False)  # noqa: E712
  if source_types:
    stmt = stmt.where(CashDelta.source_type.in_(source_types))
  rows = session.exec(stmt).all()
  if not rows:
    return None
  earliest: Optional[date] = None
  for row in rows:
    day = business_date_from_utc(row.effective_at)
    if earliest is None or day < earliest:
      earliest = day
    session.delete(row)
  return earliest


def recompute_cash_summaries(
  session: Session,
  start_business_date: date,
  end_business_date: date,
) -> None:
  if end_business_date < start_business_date:
    return
  previous = _latest_summary(session, start_business_date - timedelta(days=1))
  running_cash = previous.cash_end if previous else 0.0

  range_start = business_date_start_utc(start_business_date)
  range_end = business_date_start_utc(end_business_date + timedelta(days=1))
  deltas = session.exec(
    select(CashDelta)
    .where(CashDelta.is_deleted == False)  # noqa: E712
    .where(CashDelta.effective_at >= range_start)
    .where(CashDelta.effective_at < range_end)
    .order_by(CashDelta.effective_at, CashDelta.created_at, CashDelta.id)
  ).all()

  deltas_by_date: dict[date, list[CashDelta]] = {}
  for delta in deltas:
    date_key = business_date_from_utc(delta.effective_at)
    deltas_by_date.setdefault(date_key, []).append(delta)

  for current_date in _date_range(start_business_date, end_business_date):
    day_start = running_cash
    day_delta = 0.0
    day_rows = deltas_by_date.get(current_date, [])
    init_rows = [row for row in day_rows if row.source_type == "cash_init"]
    if init_rows:
      day_start = init_rows[0].delta_cash
      running_cash = day_start

    for delta in day_rows:
      if delta.source_type == "cash_init":
        continue
      running_cash += delta.delta_cash
      day_delta += delta.delta_cash

    day_end = running_cash
    summary = session.exec(
      select(CashDailySummary)
      .where(CashDailySummary.business_date == current_date)
    ).first()
    if summary:
      summary.cash_start = day_start
      summary.cash_delta = day_delta
      summary.cash_end = day_end
      summary.computed_at = datetime.now(timezone.utc)
      session.add(summary)
    else:
      session.add(
        CashDailySummary(
          business_date=current_date,
          cash_start=day_start,
          cash_delta=day_delta,
          cash_end=day_end,
          computed_at=datetime.now(timezone.utc),
        )
      )


def add_cash_delta(
  session: Session,
  *,
  effective_at: datetime,
  source_type: str,
  source_id: Optional[str],
  delta_cash: float,
  reason: Optional[str] = None,
  actor_id: Optional[str] = None,
  is_manual: bool = False,
) -> CashDelta:
  effective_at_norm = _to_utc_naive(effective_at)
  now = datetime.now(timezone.utc)
  delta = CashDelta(
    effective_at=effective_at_norm,
    source_type=source_type,
    source_id=source_id,
    delta_cash=delta_cash,
    reason=reason,
    is_manual=is_manual,
    created_at=now,
    created_by=actor_id,
  )
  session.add(delta)
  start_business_date = business_date_from_utc(effective_at_norm)
  end_business_date = business_date_from_utc(datetime.now(timezone.utc))
  recompute_cash_summaries(session, start_business_date, end_business_date)
  return delta

from __future__ import annotations

from datetime import date, datetime, timedelta, timezone
from typing import Optional

from sqlmodel import Session, select

from app.models import CompanyDailySummary, CompanyDelta
from app.utils.time import business_date_from_utc, business_date_start_utc, to_utc_naive


def _date_range(start: date, end: date) -> list[date]:
  if end < start:
    return []
  days = (end - start).days
  return [start + timedelta(days=offset) for offset in range(days + 1)]


def _to_utc_naive(dt: datetime) -> datetime:
  return to_utc_naive(dt)


def _latest_summary(session: Session, up_to: Optional[date] = None) -> Optional[CompanyDailySummary]:
  stmt = select(CompanyDailySummary)
  if up_to is not None:
    stmt = stmt.where(CompanyDailySummary.business_date <= up_to)
  return session.exec(stmt.order_by(CompanyDailySummary.business_date.desc())).first()


def delete_company_deltas_for_source(
  session: Session,
  *,
  source_id: str,
  source_types: Optional[list[str]] = None,
) -> Optional[date]:
  stmt = select(CompanyDelta).where(CompanyDelta.source_id == source_id)
  if source_types:
    stmt = stmt.where(CompanyDelta.source_type.in_(source_types))
  rows = session.exec(stmt).all()
  if not rows:
    return None
  earliest: Optional[date] = None
  for row in rows:
    day = business_date_from_utc(row.effective_at)
    if earliest is None or day < earliest:
      earliest = day
    session.delete(row)
  return earliest


def recompute_company_summaries(
  session: Session,
  start_business_date: date,
  end_business_date: date,
) -> None:
  if end_business_date < start_business_date:
    return
  previous = _latest_summary(session, start_business_date - timedelta(days=1))
  running_payable = previous.payable_end if previous else 0.0
  running_payable_12 = previous.payable_12kg_end if previous else 0
  running_payable_48 = previous.payable_48kg_end if previous else 0
  running_give = previous.payable_give_end if previous else 0.0
  running_receive = previous.payable_receive_end if previous else 0.0
  running_12_give = previous.payable_12kg_give_end if previous else 0
  running_12_receive = previous.payable_12kg_receive_end if previous else 0
  running_48_give = previous.payable_48kg_give_end if previous else 0
  running_48_receive = previous.payable_48kg_receive_end if previous else 0

  range_start = business_date_start_utc(start_business_date)
  range_end = business_date_start_utc(end_business_date + timedelta(days=1))
  deltas = session.exec(
    select(CompanyDelta)
    .where(CompanyDelta.effective_at >= range_start)
    .where(CompanyDelta.effective_at < range_end)
    .order_by(CompanyDelta.effective_at, CompanyDelta.created_at, CompanyDelta.id)
  ).all()

  deltas_by_date: dict[date, list[CompanyDelta]] = {}
  for delta in deltas:
    date_key = business_date_from_utc(delta.effective_at)
    deltas_by_date.setdefault(date_key, []).append(delta)

  for current_date in _date_range(start_business_date, end_business_date):
    day_start = running_payable
    day_delta = 0.0
    day_start_12 = running_payable_12
    day_start_48 = running_payable_48
    day_delta_12 = 0
    day_delta_48 = 0
    day_give_start = running_give
    day_receive_start = running_receive
    day_give_delta = 0.0
    day_receive_delta = 0.0
    day_12_give_start = running_12_give
    day_12_receive_start = running_12_receive
    day_12_give_delta = 0
    day_12_receive_delta = 0
    day_48_give_start = running_48_give
    day_48_receive_start = running_48_receive
    day_48_give_delta = 0
    day_48_receive_delta = 0
    for delta in deltas_by_date.get(current_date, []):
      running_payable += delta.delta_payable
      day_delta += delta.delta_payable
      running_payable_12 += delta.delta_12kg
      running_payable_48 += delta.delta_48kg
      day_delta_12 += delta.delta_12kg
      day_delta_48 += delta.delta_48kg
      if delta.delta_payable:
        if delta.source_type == "company_payment":
          adjustment = abs(delta.delta_payable)
          running_give = max(0.0, running_give - adjustment)
          day_give_delta -= adjustment
        elif delta.delta_payable > 0:
          running_give += delta.delta_payable
          day_give_delta += delta.delta_payable
        else:
          running_receive += abs(delta.delta_payable)
          day_receive_delta += abs(delta.delta_payable)
      if delta.delta_12kg > 0:
        running_12_receive += delta.delta_12kg
        day_12_receive_delta += delta.delta_12kg
      elif delta.delta_12kg < 0:
        running_12_give += abs(delta.delta_12kg)
        day_12_give_delta += abs(delta.delta_12kg)
      if delta.delta_48kg > 0:
        running_48_receive += delta.delta_48kg
        day_48_receive_delta += delta.delta_48kg
      elif delta.delta_48kg < 0:
        running_48_give += abs(delta.delta_48kg)
        day_48_give_delta += abs(delta.delta_48kg)
    day_end = running_payable
    day_end_12 = running_payable_12
    day_end_48 = running_payable_48
    day_give_end = running_give
    day_receive_end = running_receive
    day_12_give_end = running_12_give
    day_12_receive_end = running_12_receive
    day_48_give_end = running_48_give
    day_48_receive_end = running_48_receive
    summary = session.exec(
      select(CompanyDailySummary)
      .where(CompanyDailySummary.business_date == current_date)
    ).first()
    if summary:
      summary.payable_start = day_start
      summary.payable_delta = day_delta
      summary.payable_end = day_end
      summary.payable_12kg_start = day_start_12
      summary.payable_12kg_delta = day_delta_12
      summary.payable_12kg_end = day_end_12
      summary.payable_48kg_start = day_start_48
      summary.payable_48kg_delta = day_delta_48
      summary.payable_48kg_end = day_end_48
      summary.payable_give_start = day_give_start
      summary.payable_give_delta = day_give_delta
      summary.payable_give_end = day_give_end
      summary.payable_receive_start = day_receive_start
      summary.payable_receive_delta = day_receive_delta
      summary.payable_receive_end = day_receive_end
      summary.payable_12kg_give_start = day_12_give_start
      summary.payable_12kg_give_delta = day_12_give_delta
      summary.payable_12kg_give_end = day_12_give_end
      summary.payable_12kg_receive_start = day_12_receive_start
      summary.payable_12kg_receive_delta = day_12_receive_delta
      summary.payable_12kg_receive_end = day_12_receive_end
      summary.payable_48kg_give_start = day_48_give_start
      summary.payable_48kg_give_delta = day_48_give_delta
      summary.payable_48kg_give_end = day_48_give_end
      summary.payable_48kg_receive_start = day_48_receive_start
      summary.payable_48kg_receive_delta = day_48_receive_delta
      summary.payable_48kg_receive_end = day_48_receive_end
      summary.computed_at = datetime.now(timezone.utc)
      session.add(summary)
    else:
      session.add(
        CompanyDailySummary(
          business_date=current_date,
          payable_start=day_start,
          payable_delta=day_delta,
          payable_end=day_end,
          payable_12kg_start=day_start_12,
          payable_12kg_delta=day_delta_12,
          payable_12kg_end=day_end_12,
          payable_48kg_start=day_start_48,
          payable_48kg_delta=day_delta_48,
          payable_48kg_end=day_end_48,
          payable_give_start=day_give_start,
          payable_give_delta=day_give_delta,
          payable_give_end=day_give_end,
          payable_receive_start=day_receive_start,
          payable_receive_delta=day_receive_delta,
          payable_receive_end=day_receive_end,
          payable_12kg_give_start=day_12_give_start,
          payable_12kg_give_delta=day_12_give_delta,
          payable_12kg_give_end=day_12_give_end,
          payable_12kg_receive_start=day_12_receive_start,
          payable_12kg_receive_delta=day_12_receive_delta,
          payable_12kg_receive_end=day_12_receive_end,
          payable_48kg_give_start=day_48_give_start,
          payable_48kg_give_delta=day_48_give_delta,
          payable_48kg_give_end=day_48_give_end,
          payable_48kg_receive_start=day_48_receive_start,
          payable_48kg_receive_delta=day_48_receive_delta,
          payable_48kg_receive_end=day_48_receive_end,
          computed_at=datetime.now(timezone.utc),
        )
      )


def add_company_delta(

inventory.py
from datetime import date, datetime, timedelta, timezone
from typing import Optional, Sequence

from fastapi import HTTPException
from sqlmodel import Session, select

import logging

from app.models import InventoryDailySummary, InventoryDelta, InventoryRecalcQueue, InventoryVersion
from app.utils.locks import acquire_inventory_lock
from app.utils.time import business_date_end_utc, business_date_from_utc, business_date_start_utc, to_utc_naive


logger = logging.getLogger(__name__)


def _to_utc_naive(dt: datetime) -> datetime:
  """
  Normalize any datetime to naive UTC to avoid offset-naive vs offset-aware comparisons.
  If the datetime is timezone-aware, convert to UTC and strip tzinfo. If already naive, return as-is.
  """
  return to_utc_naive(dt)


def latest_inventory_version(session: Session, gas_type: str) -> Optional[InventoryVersion]:
  """
  Fetch the most recent InventoryVersion for a gas type, ordered by business time (effective_at) and
  creation time to guarantee deterministic pick when multiple writes land at the same instant.
  """
  return session.exec(
    select(InventoryVersion)
    .where(InventoryVersion.gas_type == gas_type)
    .order_by(InventoryVersion.effective_at.desc(), InventoryVersion.created_at.desc())
  ).first()


def _ordered_versions(session: Session, gas_type: str) -> Sequence[InventoryVersion]:
  return session.exec(
    select(InventoryVersion)
    .where(InventoryVersion.gas_type == gas_type)
    .order_by(InventoryVersion.effective_at, InventoryVersion.created_at)
  ).all()


def _recompute_chain(versions: list[InventoryVersion], deltas: dict[str, tuple[int, int]]) -> None:
  """
  Recompute cumulative counts for a gas type after inserting a backdated version.
  We keep each version's original delta (derived from the pre-change chain) so future
  states shift consistently from the new insertion point onward.
  """
  if len(versions) < 2:
    return
  full = versions[0].full_count
  empty = versions[0].empty_count
  for cur in versions[1:]:
    df, de = deltas[cur.id]
    full += df
    empty += de
    cur.full_count = full
    cur.empty_count = empty


def apply_inventory_delta(
  session: Session,
  *,
  gas_type: str,
  delta_full: int,
  delta_empty: int,
  reason: str,
  event_type: str,
  event_id: str,
  effective_at: datetime,
  allow_negative_full: bool = False,
  allow_negative_empty: bool = False,
) -> InventoryVersion:
  """
  Append a new InventoryVersion using the provided deltas. This enforces:
  - Inventory is already initialized for the gas type
  - Non-negative resulting counts (unless explicitly allowed)
  - Historical inserts are allowed: a backdated change will reflow all later versions.
  """
  effective_at_norm = _to_utc_naive(effective_at)
  versions = list(_ordered_versions(session, gas_type))
  if not versions:
    raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail="inventory_not_initialized")

  # Capture original deltas per version to preserve event impact when reflowing
  base_deltas: dict[str, tuple[int, int]] = {}
  for prev, cur in zip(versions, versions[1:]):
    base_deltas[cur.id] = (cur.full_count - prev.full_count, cur.empty_count - prev.empty_count)

  # Find insertion point (latest version with effective_at <= target, stable by created_at)
  insert_idx = None
  for idx, v in enumerate(versions):
    if _to_utc_naive(v.effective_at) <= effective_at_norm:
      insert_idx = idx
    else:
      break
  if insert_idx is None:
    # No prior records; do not allow changes before the initial inventory baseline.
    raise HTTPException(
      status_code=400,
      detail="Order date is before initial inventory. Initialize inventory for that date or change the order date.",
    )

  base = versions[insert_idx]
  new_full = base.full_count + delta_full
  new_empty = base.empty_count + delta_empty
  if (new_full < 0 and not allow_negative_full) or (new_empty < 0 and not allow_negative_empty):
    raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail="inventory_negative")

  now = datetime.now(timezone.utc)
  version = InventoryVersion(
    gas_type=gas_type,
    full_count=new_full,
    empty_count=new_empty,
    reason=reason,
    event_type=event_type,
    event_id=event_id,
    effective_at=effective_at_norm,
    created_at=now,
  )

  # Insert and reflow
  versions.insert(insert_idx + 1, version)
  base_deltas[version.id] = (delta_full, delta_empty)
  _recompute_chain(versions, base_deltas)
  for v in versions:
    session.add(v)
  return version


def get_inventory_warnings(session: Session) -> list[dict[str, object]]:
  """
  Scan inventory history for negative full counts and suggest a ghost refill
  on the first date a gas type went negative.
  """
  negatives = session.exec(
    select(InventoryVersion)
    .where(InventoryVersion.full_count < 0)
    .order_by(InventoryVersion.effective_at)
  ).all()
  first_by_gas: dict[str, InventoryVersion] = {}
  for version in negatives:
    if version.gas_type not in first_by_gas:
      first_by_gas[version.gas_type] = version

  warnings: list[dict[str, object]] = []
  for gas_type, version in first_by_gas.items():
    warnings.append(
      {
        "gas_type": gas_type,
        "date": version.effective_at.date().isoformat(),
        "suggested_refill_full": abs(version.full_count),
        "message": "ghost_refill_suggested",
      }
    )
  return warnings


def _date_range(start: date, end: date) -> list[date]:
  if end < start:
    return []
  days = (end - start).days
  return [start + timedelta(days=offset) for offset in range(days + 1)]


def _latest_summary_for_gas(
  session: Session, gas_type: str, up_to: Optional[date] = None
) -> Optional[InventoryDailySummary]:
  stmt = select(InventoryDailySummary).where(InventoryDailySummary.gas_type == gas_type)
  if up_to is not None:
    stmt = stmt.where(InventoryDailySummary.business_date <= up_to)
  return session.exec(stmt.order_by(InventoryDailySummary.business_date.desc())).first()


def latest_inventory_snapshot(session: Session) -> Optional[dict[str, object]]:
  today = business_date_from_utc(datetime.now(timezone.utc))
  summary_12 = _latest_summary_for_gas(session, "12kg", today)
  summary_48 = _latest_summary_for_gas(session, "48kg", today)
  if not summary_12 and not summary_48:
    return None
  full12 = summary_12.day_end_full if summary_12 else 0
  empty12 = summary_12.day_end_empty if summary_12 else 0
  full48 = summary_48.day_end_full if summary_48 else 0
  empty48 = summary_48.day_end_empty if summary_48 else 0
  date_candidates = [s.business_date for s in (summary_12, summary_48) if s]
  as_of = business_date_end_utc(max(date_candidates)) if date_candidates else datetime.now(timezone.utc)
  return {
    "as_of": as_of,
    "full12": full12,
    "empty12": empty12,
    "total12": full12 + empty12,
    "full48": full48,
    "empty48": empty48,
    "total48": full48 + empty48,
    "reason": None,
  }


def inventory_totals_at(session: Session, gas_type: str, effective_at: datetime) -> tuple[int, int]:
  effective_at_norm = _to_utc_naive(effective_at)
  business_date = business_date_from_utc(effective_at_norm)
  previous = session.exec(
    select(InventoryDailySummary)
    .where(InventoryDailySummary.gas_type == gas_type)
    .where(InventoryDailySummary.business_date < business_date)
    .order_by(InventoryDailySummary.business_date.desc())
  ).first()
  full = previous.day_end_full if previous else 0
  empty = previous.day_end_empty if previous else 0

  has_any = session.exec(
    select(InventoryDelta.id)
    .where(InventoryDelta.gas_type == gas_type)
    .where(InventoryDelta.is_deleted == False)  # noqa: E712
    .limit(1)
  ).first()
  if not has_any and not previous:
    raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail="inventory_not_initialized")

  if previous is None:
    deltas = session.exec(
      select(InventoryDelta)
      .where(InventoryDelta.gas_type == gas_type)
      .where(InventoryDelta.is_deleted == False)  # noqa: E712
      .where(InventoryDelta.effective_at <= effective_at_norm)
      .order_by(InventoryDelta.effective_at, InventoryDelta.created_at, InventoryDelta.id)
    ).all()
    for delta in deltas:
      full += delta.delta_full
      empty += delta.delta_empty
    return full, empty

  day_start = business_date_start_utc(business_date)
  next_day = business_date_start_utc(business_date + timedelta(days=1))
  deltas = session.exec(
    select(InventoryDelta)
    .where(InventoryDelta.gas_type == gas_type)
    .where(InventoryDelta.is_deleted == False)  # noqa: E712
    .where(InventoryDelta.effective_at >= day_start)
    .where(InventoryDelta.effective_at < next_day)
    .where(InventoryDelta.effective_at <= effective_at_norm)
    .order_by(InventoryDelta.effective_at, InventoryDelta.created_at, InventoryDelta.id)
  ).all()
  for delta in deltas:
    full += delta.delta_full
    empty += delta.delta_empty
  return full, empty


def inventory_totals_before_source(
  session: Session,
  *,
  gas_type: str,
  source_type: str,
  source_id: str,
) -> tuple[int, int]:
  has_any = session.exec(
    select(InventoryDelta.id)
    .where(InventoryDelta.gas_type == gas_type)
    .where(InventoryDelta.is_deleted == False)  # noqa: E712
    .limit(1)
  ).first()
  if not has_any:
    raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail="inventory_not_initialized")

  full = 0
  empty = 0
  deltas = session.exec(
    select(InventoryDelta)
    .where(InventoryDelta.gas_type == gas_type)
    .where(InventoryDelta.is_deleted == False)  # noqa: E712
    .order_by(InventoryDelta.effective_at, InventoryDelta.created_at, InventoryDelta.id)
  ).all()
  for delta in deltas:
    if delta.source_type == source_type and delta.source_id == source_id:
      break
    full += delta.delta_full
    empty += delta.delta_empty
  return full, empty


def enqueue_recalc_job(session: Session, gas_type: str, start_business_date: date) -> InventoryRecalcQueue:
  now = datetime.now(timezone.utc)
  existing = session.exec(
    select(InventoryRecalcQueue)
    .where(InventoryRecalcQueue.gas_type == gas_type)
    .where(InventoryRecalcQueue.status == "pending")
    .order_by(InventoryRecalcQueue.created_at.desc())
  ).first()
  if existing:
    if start_business_date < existing.start_business_date:
      existing.start_business_date = start_business_date
      existing.updated_at = now
      session.add(existing)
    return existing

  job = InventoryRecalcQueue(
    gas_type=gas_type,
    start_business_date=start_business_date,
    status="pending",
    created_at=now,
    updated_at=now,
  )
  session.add(job)
  return job


def delete_inventory_deltas_for_source(
  session: Session,
  *,
  source_id: str,
  source_types: Optional[list[str]] = None,
) -> dict[str, date]:
  stmt = select(InventoryDelta).where(InventoryDelta.source_id == source_id)
  stmt = stmt.where(InventoryDelta.is_deleted == False)  # noqa: E712
  if source_types:
    stmt = stmt.where(InventoryDelta.source_type.in_(source_types))
  rows = session.exec(stmt).all()
  earliest: dict[str, date] = {}
  for row in rows:
    day = business_date_from_utc(row.effective_at)
    existing = earliest.get(row.gas_type)
    if existing is None or day < existing:
      earliest[row.gas_type] = day
    session.delete(row)
  return earliest


def soft_delete_inventory_deltas_for_source(
  session: Session,
  *,
  source_id: str,
  source_types: Optional[list[str]] = None,
) -> dict[str, date]:
  stmt = select(InventoryDelta).where(InventoryDelta.source_id == source_id)
  stmt = stmt.where(InventoryDelta.is_deleted == False)  # noqa: E712
  if source_types:
    stmt = stmt.where(InventoryDelta.source_type.in_(source_types))
  rows = session.exec(stmt).all()
  earliest: dict[str, date] = {}
  deleted_at = datetime.now(timezone.utc)
  for row in rows:
    day = business_date_from_utc(row.effective_at)
    existing = earliest.get(row.gas_type)
    if existing is None or day < existing:
      earliest[row.gas_type] = day
    row.is_deleted = True
    row.deleted_at = deleted_at
    row.updated_at = deleted_at
    session.add(row)
  return earliest


def recompute_daily_summaries(
  session: Session,
  gas_type: str,
  start_business_date: date,
  end_business_date: date,
  *,
  allow_negative: bool = False,
) -> None:
  acquire_inventory_lock(session, gas_type)
  if end_business_date < start_business_date:
    return
  previous = session.exec(
    select(InventoryDailySummary)
    .where(InventoryDailySummary.gas_type == gas_type)
    .where(InventoryDailySummary.business_date < start_business_date)
    .order_by(InventoryDailySummary.business_date.desc())
  ).first()
  running_full = previous.day_end_full if previous else 0
  running_empty = previous.day_end_empty if previous else 0

  range_start = business_date_start_utc(start_business_date)
  range_end = business_date_start_utc(end_business_date + timedelta(days=1))
  deltas = session.exec(
    select(InventoryDelta)
    .where(InventoryDelta.gas_type == gas_type)
    .where(InventoryDelta.is_deleted == False)  # noqa: E712
    .where(InventoryDelta.effective_at >= range_start)
    .where(InventoryDelta.effective_at < range_end)
    .order_by(InventoryDelta.effective_at, InventoryDelta.created_at, InventoryDelta.id)
  ).all()

  deltas_by_date: dict[date, list[InventoryDelta]] = {}
  for delta in deltas:
    date_key = business_date_from_utc(delta.effective_at)
    deltas_by_date.setdefault(date_key, []).append(delta)

  for current_date in _date_range(start_business_date, end_business_date):
    day_start_full = running_full
    day_start_empty = running_empty
    for delta in deltas_by_date.get(current_date, []):
      running_full += delta.delta_full
      running_empty += delta.delta_empty
      if running_full < 0 or running_empty < 0:
        if allow_negative:
          logger.warning(
            "inventory_negative gas=%s date=%s full=%s empty=%s",
            gas_type,
            current_date,
            running_full,
            running_empty,
          )
        else:
          raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail="inventory_negative")

    day_end_full = running_full
    day_end_empty = running_empty
    summary = session.exec(
      select(InventoryDailySummary)
      .where(InventoryDailySummary.gas_type == gas_type)
      .where(InventoryDailySummary.business_date == current_date)
    ).first()
    if summary:
      summary.day_start_full = day_start_full
      summary.day_start_empty = day_start_empty
      summary.day_delta_full = day_end_full - day_start_full
      summary.day_delta_empty = day_end_empty - day_start_empty
      summary.day_end_full = day_end_full
      summary.day_end_empty = day_end_empty
      summary.computed_at = datetime.now(timezone.utc)
      session.add(summary)
    else:
      session.add(
        InventoryDailySummary(
          business_date=current_date,
          gas_type=gas_type,
          day_start_full=day_start_full,
          day_start_empty=day_start_empty,
          day_delta_full=day_end_full - day_start_full,
          day_delta_empty=day_end_empty - day_start_empty,
          day_end_full=day_end_full,
          day_end_empty=day_end_empty,
          computed_at=datetime.now(timezone.utc),
        )
      )


def _insert_inventory_delta(
  session: Session,
  *,
  gas_type: str,
  delta_full: int,
  delta_empty: int,
  effective_at: datetime,
  source_type: str,
  source_id: Optional[str] = None,
  reason: Optional[str] = None,
  actor_id: Optional[str] = None,
  is_manual: bool = False,
) -> InventoryDelta:
  effective_at_norm = _to_utc_naive(effective_at)
  now = datetime.now(timezone.utc)
  delta = InventoryDelta(
    gas_type=gas_type,
    delta_full=delta_full,
    delta_empty=delta_empty,
    effective_at=effective_at_norm,
    source_type=source_type,
    source_id=source_id,
    reason=reason,
    is_manual=is_manual,
    created_at=now,
    created_by=actor_id,
  )
  session.add(delta)
  return delta


def add_inventory_delta(
  session: Session,
  *,
  gas_type: str,
  delta_full: int,
  delta_empty: int,
  effective_at: datetime,
  source_type: str,
  source_id: Optional[str] = None,
  reason: Optional[str] = None,
  actor_id: Optional[str] = None,
  allow_negative: bool = False,
  is_manual: bool = False,
) -> InventoryDelta:
  effective_at_norm = _to_utc_naive(effective_at)
  if source_type != "init":
    has_any = session.exec(
      select(InventoryDelta.id)
      .where(InventoryDelta.gas_type == gas_type)
      .where(InventoryDelta.is_deleted == False)  # noqa: E712
      .limit(1)
    ).first()
    if not has_any:
      raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail="inventory_not_initialized")

  acquire_inventory_lock(session, gas_type)
  delta = _insert_inventory_delta(
    session,
    gas_type=gas_type,
    delta_full=delta_full,
    delta_empty=delta_empty,
    effective_at=effective_at_norm,
    source_type=source_type,
    source_id=source_id,
    reason=reason,
    actor_id=actor_id,
    is_manual=is_manual,
  )

  start_business_date = business_date_from_utc(effective_at_norm)
  enqueue_recalc_job(session, gas_type, start_business_date)
  end_business_date = business_date_from_utc(datetime.now(timezone.utc))
  recompute_daily_summaries(
    session,
    gas_type,
    start_business_date,
    end_business_date,
    allow_negative=allow_negative,
  )
  return delta

customers.py
from datetime import date, datetime, timezone

from sqlmodel import Session, select

from app.models import CollectionEvent, Customer, CustomerAdjustment, Order
from app.utils.time import business_date_start_utc, to_utc_naive


def sync_customer_totals(session: Session, customer_id: str) -> None:
  customer = session.get(Customer, customer_id)
  if not customer or customer.is_deleted:
    return

  orders = session.exec(
    select(Order).where(Order.customer_id == customer_id, Order.is_deleted == False)  # noqa: E712
  ).all()
  collections = session.exec(
    select(CollectionEvent).where(
      CollectionEvent.customer_id == customer_id,
      CollectionEvent.is_deleted == False,  # noqa: E712
    )
  ).all()
  adjustments = session.exec(
    select(CustomerAdjustment).where(CustomerAdjustment.customer_id == customer_id)
  ).all()

  def order_net_paid(order: Order) -> float:
    return order.paid_amount or 0

  order_money = sum(
    order.price_total - order_net_paid(order)
    for order in orders
  )
  adjust_money = sum(adj.amount_money for adj in adjustments)
  collection_money = sum(
    (ev.amount_money or 0)
    for ev in collections
    if ev.action_type == "payment"
  )
  money_balance = order_money + adjust_money - collection_money

  money_to_receive = 0.0
  money_to_give = 0.0
  for order in orders:
    delta = order.price_total - order_net_paid(order)
    if delta >= 0:
      money_to_receive += delta
    else:
      money_to_give += abs(delta)
  for adj in adjustments:
    if adj.amount_money_to_receive or adj.amount_money_to_give:
      money_to_receive += adj.amount_money_to_receive
      money_to_give += adj.amount_money_to_give
    else:
      if adj.amount_money >= 0:
        money_to_receive += adj.amount_money
      else:
        money_to_give += abs(adj.amount_money)
  for ev in collections:
    if ev.action_type != "payment":
      continue
    delta = -(ev.amount_money or 0)
    if delta >= 0:
      money_to_receive += delta
    else:
      money_to_give += abs(delta)

  order_count = len(orders)
  total_cylinders = sum(order.cylinders_installed for order in orders)

  order_12 = sum(
    order.cylinders_installed - order.cylinders_received
    for order in orders
    if order.gas_type == "12kg"
  )
  order_48 = sum(
    order.cylinders_installed - order.cylinders_received
    for order in orders
    if order.gas_type == "48kg"
  )
  adjust_12 = sum(adj.count_12kg for adj in adjustments)
  adjust_48 = sum(adj.count_48kg for adj in adjustments)

  customer.money_balance = money_balance
  customer.money_to_receive = money_to_receive
  customer.money_to_give = money_to_give
  customer.total_cylinders_delivered_lifetime = total_cylinders
  customer.order_count = order_count
  collection_12 = sum(
    (ev.qty_12kg or 0)
    for ev in collections
    if ev.action_type == "return"
  )
  collection_48 = sum(
    (ev.qty_48kg or 0)
    for ev in collections
    if ev.action_type == "return"
  )
  customer.cylinder_balance_12kg = order_12 + adjust_12 - collection_12
  customer.cylinder_balance_48kg = order_48 + adjust_48 - collection_48
  cyl_receive_12 = 0
  cyl_give_12 = 0
  cyl_receive_48 = 0
  cyl_give_48 = 0
  for order in orders:
    delta = order.cylinders_installed - order.cylinders_received
    if order.gas_type == "12kg":
      if delta >= 0:
        cyl_receive_12 += delta
      else:
        cyl_give_12 += abs(delta)
    elif order.gas_type == "48kg":
      if delta >= 0:
        cyl_receive_48 += delta
      else:
        cyl_give_48 += abs(delta)
  for adj in adjustments:
    if adj.count_12kg_to_receive or adj.count_12kg_to_give:
      cyl_receive_12 += adj.count_12kg_to_receive
      cyl_give_12 += adj.count_12kg_to_give
    else:
      if adj.count_12kg >= 0:
        cyl_receive_12 += adj.count_12kg
      else:
        cyl_give_12 += abs(adj.count_12kg)
    if adj.count_48kg_to_receive or adj.count_48kg_to_give:
      cyl_receive_48 += adj.count_48kg_to_receive
      cyl_give_48 += adj.count_48kg_to_give
    else:
      if adj.count_48kg >= 0:
        cyl_receive_48 += adj.count_48kg
      else:
        cyl_give_48 += abs(adj.count_48kg)
  for ev in collections:
    if ev.action_type != "return":
      continue
    delta_12 = -(ev.qty_12kg or 0)
    delta_48 = -(ev.qty_48kg or 0)
    if delta_12 >= 0:
      cyl_receive_12 += delta_12
    else:
      cyl_give_12 += abs(delta_12)
    if delta_48 >= 0:
      cyl_receive_48 += delta_48
    else:
      cyl_give_48 += abs(delta_48)
  customer.cylinder_to_receive_12kg = cyl_receive_12
  customer.cylinder_to_give_12kg = cyl_give_12
  customer.cylinder_to_receive_48kg = cyl_receive_48
  customer.cylinder_to_give_48kg = cyl_give_48
  customer.updated_at = datetime.now(timezone.utc)
  session.add(customer)


def rebuild_customer_ledger(
  session: Session,
  *,
  customer_id: str,
  start_date: datetime | date,
) -> None:
  customer = session.get(Customer, customer_id)
  if not customer or customer.is_deleted:
    return

  if isinstance(start_date, date) and not isinstance(start_date, datetime):
    start_dt = business_date_start_utc(start_date)
  else:
    start_dt = to_utc_naive(start_date)

  def order_net_paid(order: Order) -> float:
    return order.paid_amount or 0

  orders_before = session.exec(
    select(Order)
    .where(Order.customer_id == customer_id, Order.is_deleted == False)  # noqa: E712
    .where(Order.delivered_at < start_dt)
  ).all()
  collections_before = session.exec(
    select(CollectionEvent)
    .where(CollectionEvent.customer_id == customer_id, CollectionEvent.is_deleted == False)  # noqa: E712
    .where(CollectionEvent.effective_at < start_dt)
  ).all()
  adjustments_before = session.exec(
    select(CustomerAdjustment)
    .where(CustomerAdjustment.customer_id == customer_id)
    .where(CustomerAdjustment.created_at < start_dt)
  ).all()

  money_before = sum(order.price_total - order_net_paid(order) for order in orders_before)
  money_before += sum(adj.amount_money for adj in adjustments_before)
  money_before -= sum(
    (ev.amount_money or 0)
    for ev in collections_before
    if ev.action_type == "payment"
  )

  cyl_before_12 = sum(
    order.cylinders_installed - order.cylinders_received
    for order in orders_before
    if order.gas_type == "12kg"
  )
  cyl_before_48 = sum(
    order.cylinders_installed - order.cylinders_received
    for order in orders_before
    if order.gas_type == "48kg"
  )
  cyl_before_12 += sum(adj.count_12kg for adj in adjustments_before)
  cyl_before_48 += sum(adj.count_48kg for adj in adjustments_before)
  cyl_before_12 -= sum(
    (ev.qty_12kg or 0)
    for ev in collections_before
    if ev.action_type == "return"
  )
  cyl_before_48 -= sum(
    (ev.qty_48kg or 0)
    for ev in collections_before
    if ev.action_type == "return"
  )

  running_money = money_before
  running_cyl_12 = cyl_before_12
  running_cyl_48 = cyl_before_48

  orders = session.exec(
    select(Order)
    .where(Order.customer_id == customer_id, Order.is_deleted == False)  # noqa: E712
    .where(Order.delivered_at >= start_dt)
  ).all()
  collections = session.exec(
    select(CollectionEvent)
    .where(CollectionEvent.customer_id == customer_id, CollectionEvent.is_deleted == False)  # noqa: E712
    .where(CollectionEvent.effective_at >= start_dt)
  ).all()
  adjustments = session.exec(
    select(CustomerAdjustment)
    .where(CustomerAdjustment.customer_id == customer_id)
    .where(CustomerAdjustment.created_at >= start_dt)
  ).all()

  timeline: list[tuple[datetime, datetime, str, object]] = []
  for order in orders:
    timeline.append((to_utc_naive(order.delivered_at), to_utc_naive(order.created_at), "order", order))
  for ev in collections:
    timeline.append((to_utc_naive(ev.effective_at), to_utc_naive(ev.created_at), "collection", ev))
  for adj in adjustments:
    timeline.append((to_utc_naive(adj.created_at), to_utc_naive(adj.created_at), "adjustment", adj))

  timeline.sort(key=lambda item: (item[0], item[1]))
  now = datetime.now(timezone.utc)

  for _, _, kind, record in timeline:
    if kind == "order":
      order = record
      order.money_balance_before = running_money
      gross_paid = order_net_paid(order)
      running_money += order.price_total - gross_paid
      order.money_balance_after = running_money

      order.cyl_balance_before = {
        "12kg": running_cyl_12,
        "48kg": running_cyl_48,
      }
      cyl_delta = order.cylinders_installed - order.cylinders_received
      if order.gas_type == "12kg":
        running_cyl_12 += cyl_delta
      elif order.gas_type == "48kg":
        running_cyl_48 += cyl_delta
      order.cyl_balance_after = {
        "12kg": running_cyl_12,
        "48kg": running_cyl_48,
      }
      order.updated_at = now
      session.add(order)
      continue

    if kind == "collection":
      ev = record
      ev.money_balance_before = running_money
      ev.cyl_balance_before = {
        "12kg": running_cyl_12,
        "48kg": running_cyl_48,
      }
      if ev.action_type == "payment":
        running_money -= ev.amount_money or 0
      else:
        running_cyl_12 -= ev.qty_12kg or 0
        running_cyl_48 -= ev.qty_48kg or 0
      ev.money_balance_after = running_money
      ev.cyl_balance_after = {
        "12kg": running_cyl_12,
        "48kg": running_cyl_48,
      }
      ev.updated_at = now
      session.add(ev)
      continue

    adj = record
    running_money += adj.amount_money
    running_cyl_12 += adj.count_12kg
    running_cyl_48 += adj.count_48kg

  sync_customer_totals(session, customer.id)
Deleted
company.py
from datetime import datetime, timedelta, timezone
from typing import Optional

from fastapi import APIRouter, Depends, HTTPException, status
from sqlmodel import Session

from app.auth import get_optional_user
from app.db import get_session
from app.events import add_activity
from app.models import CompanyPayment, CompanyCylinderPaymentEvent
from app.schemas import CompanyPaymentCreate, CompanyCylinderPaymentCreate, CompanyCylinderPaymentDetails, new_id
from app.services.cash import add_cash_delta
from app.services.company import add_company_delta, recompute_company_summaries
from app.utils.time import business_date_start_utc, to_utc_naive, business_local_datetime_from_utc, business_date_from_utc

router = APIRouter(prefix="/company", tags=["company"])


@router.post("/payments", status_code=status.HTTP_201_CREATED)
def create_company_payment(payload: CompanyPaymentCreate, session: Session = Depends(get_session)) -> dict[str, object]:
  try:
    day = datetime.fromisoformat(payload.date).date()
  except ValueError as exc:
    raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail="Invalid date format") from exc
  if payload.amount <= 0:
    raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail="amount_must_be_positive")

  base = business_date_start_utc(day)
  if payload.time_of_day == "morning":
    effective_at = base + timedelta(hours=9)
  elif payload.time_of_day == "evening":
    effective_at = base + timedelta(hours=18)
  else:
    effective_at = base + timedelta(hours=12)

  payment_id = new_id("compay_")
  payment = CompanyPayment(
    id=payment_id,
    business_date=day,
    time_of_day=payload.time_of_day,
    effective_at=effective_at,
    amount=payload.amount,
    note=payload.note,
    created_at=datetime.utcnow(),
    is_deleted=False,
  )
  add_cash_delta(
    session,
    effective_at=effective_at,
    source_type="company_payment",
    source_id=payment_id,
    delta_cash=-payload.amount,
    reason=payload.note,
  )
  add_company_delta(
    session,
    effective_at=effective_at,
    source_type="company_payment",
    source_id=payment_id,
    delta_payable=-payload.amount,
    reason=payload.note,
  )
  session.add(payment)
  session.commit()
  # TODO: if payment edits/deletes are introduced, delete cash/company deltas and recompute forward.
  return {"id": payment_id, "effective_at": effective_at, "amount": payload.amount}


@router.post("/settle-cylinder-debt", response_model=CompanyCylinderPaymentDetails, status_code=status.HTTP_201_CREATED)
def settle_cylinder_debt(
  payload: CompanyCylinderPaymentCreate,
  session: Session = Depends(get_session),
  user_id: Optional[str] = Depends(get_optional_user),
) -> CompanyCylinderPaymentDetails:
  try:
    day = datetime.fromisoformat(payload.date).date()
  except ValueError as exc:
    raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail="Invalid date format") from exc

  if payload.effective_at:
    boundary = to_utc_naive(payload.effective_at)
  elif payload.time:
    try:
      parsed_time = datetime.strptime(payload.time, "%H:%M").time()
    except ValueError as exc:
      raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail="Invalid time format") from exc
    boundary = business_date_start_utc(day) + timedelta(hours=parsed_time.hour, minutes=parsed_time.minute)
  elif payload.time_of_day:
    base = datetime.combine(day, datetime.min.time())
    boundary = base + (timedelta(hours=9) if payload.time_of_day == "morning" else timedelta(hours=18))
  else:
    # Default to midday if no specific time is given
    boundary = business_date_start_utc(day) + timedelta(hours=12)

  if payload.quantity <= 0:
    raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail="quantity_must_be_positive")
  if payload.amount <= 0:
    raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail="amount_must_be_positive")

  payment_id = new_id("ccpes_")
  cylinder_payment_event = CompanyCylinderPaymentEvent(
    id=payment_id,
    business_date=day,
    effective_at=boundary,
    gas_type=payload.gas_type,
    quantity=payload.quantity,
    amount=payload.amount,
    note=payload.note,
    created_at=datetime.now(timezone.utc),
    created_by=user_id,
  )
  session.add(cylinder_payment_event)

  # Reduce cash
  add_cash_delta(
    session,
    effective_at=boundary,
    source_type="company_cylinder_payment",
    source_id=payment_id,
    delta_cash=-payload.amount,
    reason=payload.note or f"Paid for lost {payload.gas_type} cylinder debt",
    actor_id=user_id,
  )

  # Reduce company cylinder debt (payload.quantity is positive, so we increase net toward credit)
  if payload.gas_type == "12kg":
    delta_12kg = payload.quantity
    delta_48kg = 0
  else:
    delta_12kg = 0
    delta_48kg = payload.quantity

  add_company_delta(
    session,
    effective_at=boundary,
    source_type="company_cylinder_payment",
    source_id=payment_id,
    delta_payable=0, # This payment only affects cylinders, not money payable directly
    delta_12kg=delta_12kg,
    delta_48kg=delta_48kg,
    reason=payload.note or f"Settled lost {payload.gas_type} cylinder debt",
    actor_id=user_id,
  )
  session.commit()

  # Recompute company summaries from the day of the event forward
  recompute_company_summaries(session, business_date_from_utc(boundary), business_date_from_utc(datetime.now(timezone.utc)))
  
  add_activity(
    session,
    "company_cylinder_payment",
    "created",
    (
      f"Settled {payload.quantity}x {payload.gas_type} cylinder debt "
      f"with {payload.amount} at {business_local_datetime_from_utc(boundary).strftime('%H:%M')} "
      f"on {day.isoformat()}"
    ),
    payment_id,
    metadata=(
      f"date={day.isoformat()};time={business_local_datetime_from_utc(boundary).strftime('%H:%M')};"
      f"gas_type={payload.gas_type};quantity={payload.quantity};amount={payload.amount}"
    ),
  )
  session.commit()
  return CompanyCylinderPaymentDetails(
    id=payment_id,
    business_date=day.isoformat(),
    effective_at=boundary,
    gas_type=payload.gas_type,
    quantity=payload.quantity,
    amount=payload.amount,
    note=payload.note,
    is_deleted=False,
    deleted_at=None,
    created_at=cylinder_payment_event.created_at,
    created_by=cylinder_payment_event.created_by,
  )

import {
  Activity,
  ActivitySchema,
  Customer,
  SystemUpdateInput,
  CompanyCylinderPaymentCreate,
  CompanyCylinderPaymentDetails,
  CompanyCylinderPaymentDetailsSchema,
} from "@/types/domain";

function buildHappenedAt(input?: {
  date?: string;
  time?: string;
  time_of_day?: "morning" | "evening";
  at?: string;
}): string | undefined {
  if (!input) return undefined;
  if (input.at) return input.at;
  if (!input.date) return undefined;
  const time = input.time
    ? input.time
    : input.time_of_day === "morning"
      ? "09:00"
      : input.time_of_day === "evening"
        ? "18:00"
        : "12:00";
  const dt = new Date(${input.date}T${time}:00);
  return Number.isNaN(dt.getTime()) ? undefined : dt.toISOString();
}

useCompany.ts
import { useMutation, useQueryClient } from "@tanstack/react-query";
import { AxiosError } from "axios";

import { settleCompanyCylinderDebt } from "@/lib/api";
import { showToast } from "@/lib/toast";
import { CompanyCylinderPaymentCreate, CompanyCylinderPaymentDetails } from "@/types/domain";

function extractErrorMessage(err: AxiosError) {
  const detail = err.response?.data?.detail ?? err.response?.data?.message ?? err.message;
  if (typeof detail === "string") return detail;
  if (detail) return JSON.stringify(detail);
  return "Unknown error";
}

export function useSettleCompanyCylinderDebt() {
  const queryClient = useQueryClient();
  return useMutation<CompanyCylinderPaymentDetails, AxiosError, CompanyCylinderPaymentCreate>({
    mutationFn: (payload) => settleCompanyCylinderDebt(payload),
    onError: (err) => {
      const message = extractErrorMessage(err);
      showToast(Failed to settle cylinder debt: ${message});
    },
    onSuccess: () => {
      showToast("Cylinder debt settled");
      queryClient.invalidateQueries({ queryKey: ["cash"] });
      queryClient.invalidateQueries({ queryKey: ["activities"] });
      queryClient.invalidateQueries({ queryKey: ["reports-v2"], exact: false });
      queryClient.invalidateQueries({ queryKey: ["reports-day-v2"], exact: false });
    },
  });
}
