SettleCylinderDebtModal.tsx
import { Ionicons } from "@expo/vector-icons";
import { useEffect, useMemo, useRef, useState } from "react";
import {
  Alert,
  Keyboard,
  KeyboardAvoidingView,
  Modal,
  Platform,
  Pressable,
  ScrollView,
  StyleSheet,
  Text,
  TextInput,
  View,
} from "react-native";

import { gasColor } from "@/constants/gas";
import { useSettleCompanyCylinderDebt } from "@/hooks/useCompany"; // Will create this hook
import { CalendarModal, TimePickerModal } from "@/components/AddRefillModal"; // Re-use these modals

type SettleCylinderDebtModalProps = {
  visible: boolean;
  onClose: () => void;
  onSaved: () => void;
  accessoryId?: string;
};

function getNowDate() {
  const now = new Date();
  const year = now.getFullYear();
  const month = String(now.getMonth() + 1).padStart(2, "0");
  const day = String(now.getDate()).padStart(2, "0");
  return ${year}-${month}-${day};
}

function getNowTime() {
  const now = new Date();
  const hour = String(now.getHours()).padStart(2, "0");
  const minute = String(now.getMinutes()).padStart(2, "0");
  return ${hour}:${minute};
}

export function SettleCylinderDebtForm({
  visible,
  onClose,
  onSaved,
  accessoryId,
}: SettleCylinderDebtModalProps) {
  const settleDebt = useSettleCompanyCylinderDebt(); // Will use this hook
  const [date, setDate] = useState(getNowDate());
  const [time, setTime] = useState(getNowTime());
  const [calendarOpen, setCalendarOpen] = useState(false);
  const [timeOpen, setTimeOpen] = useState(false);
  const [gasType, setGasType] = useState<"12kg" | "48kg">("12kg");
  const [quantity, setQuantity] = useState("");
  const [amount, setAmount] = useState("");
  const [note, setNote] = useState("");

  useEffect(() => {
    if (!visible) {
        // Reset form when modal closes
        setDate(getNowDate());
        setTime(getNowTime());
        setGasType("12kg");
        setQuantity("");
        setAmount("");
        setNote("");
    }
  }, [visible]);

  const handleSave = async () => {
    const qtyValue = Number(quantity);
    const amountValue = Number(amount);

    if (qtyValue <= 0) {
      Alert.alert("Invalid Quantity", "Quantity must be a positive number.");
      return;
    }
    if (amountValue <= 0) {
      Alert.alert("Invalid Amount", "Amount must be a positive number.");
      return;
    }

    try {
      await settleDebt.mutateAsync({
        date,
        time,
        gas_type: gasType,
        quantity: qtyValue,
        amount: amountValue,
        note: note.trim() ? note.trim() : undefined,
      });
      Keyboard.dismiss();
      onSaved();
      onClose();
    } catch (err: any) {
      Alert.alert("Settlement Failed", err?.response?.data?.detail ?? "Failed to settle cylinder debt.");
    }
  };

  return (
    <>
      <View style={styles.modalCard}>
        <View style={styles.headerRow}>
          <Text style={styles.title}>Settle Cylinder Debt</Text>
          <Pressable onPress={onClose}>
            <Ionicons name="close" size={20} color="#0f172a" />
          </Pressable>
        </View>

        <ScrollView contentContainerStyle={styles.content} keyboardShouldPersistTaps="handled">
          <View style={styles.section}>
            <Text style={styles.label}>Date & Time</Text>
            <View style={styles.row}>
              <Pressable style={styles.dateField} onPress={() => setCalendarOpen(true)}>
                <Text style={styles.dateText}>{date}</Text>
                <Ionicons name="calendar-outline" size={16} color="#0a7ea4" />
              </Pressable>
              <Pressable style={styles.dateField} onPress={() => setTimeOpen(true)}>
                <Text style={styles.dateText}>{time}</Text>
                <Ionicons name="time-outline" size={16} color="#0a7ea4" />
              </Pressable>
              <Pressable
                style={styles.nowButton}
                onPress={() => {
                  setDate(getNowDate());
                  setTime(getNowTime());
                }}
              >
                <Text style={styles.nowButtonText}>Now</Text>
              </Pressable>
            </View>
          </View>

          <View style={styles.section}>
            <Text style={styles.label}>Cylinder Type</Text>
            <View style={styles.gasTypeRow}>
              {(["12kg", "48kg"] as const).map((type) => (
                <Pressable
                  key={type}
                  style={[styles.gasTypeButton, gasType === type && styles.gasTypeActive]}
                  onPress={() => setGasType(type)}
                >
                  <Text style={[styles.gasTypeButtonText, gasType === type && styles.gasTypeActiveText]}>
                    {type}
                  </Text>
                </Pressable>
              ))}
            </View>
          </View>

          <View style={styles.section}>
            <Text style={styles.label}>Quantity of Cylinders to Settle</Text>
            <TextInput
              style={styles.input}
              placeholder="0"
              keyboardType="numeric"
              value={quantity}
              onChangeText={setQuantity}
              inputAccessoryViewID={accessoryId}
            />
          </View>

          <View style={styles.section}>
            <Text style={styles.label}>Amount Paid (₪)</Text>
            <TextInput
              style={styles.input}
              placeholder="0"
              keyboardType="numeric"
              value={amount}
              onChangeText={setAmount}
              inputAccessoryViewID={accessoryId}
            />
          </View>

          <View style={styles.section}>
            <Text style={styles.label}>Note</Text>
            <TextInput
              style={styles.input}
              placeholder="Optional notes for settlement"
              value={note}
              onChangeText={setNote}
              inputAccessoryViewID={accessoryId}
              multiline
              numberOfLines={3}
            />
          </View>
        </ScrollView>

        <View style={styles.footerActions}>
          <Pressable style={styles.secondaryBtn} onPress={onClose}>
            <Text style={styles.secondaryText}>Cancel</Text>
          </Pressable>
          <Pressable
            style={[styles.primaryBtn, settleDebt.isPending && styles.disabledBtn]}
            onPress={handleSave}
            disabled={settleDebt.isPending}
          >
            <Text style={styles.primaryText}>{settleDebt.isPending ? "Saving..." : "Settle Debt"}</Text>
          </Pressable>
        </View>
      </View>

      <CalendarModal
        visible={calendarOpen}
        value={date}
        onSelect={(next) => {
          setDate(next);
          setCalendarOpen(false);
        }}
        onClose={() => setCalendarOpen(false)}
      />
      <TimePickerModal
        visible={timeOpen}
        value={time}
        onSelect={(next) => {
          setTime(next);
          setTimeOpen(false);
        }}
        onClose={() => setTimeOpen(false)}
      />
    </>
  );
}

export default function SettleCylinderDebtModal({
  visible,
  onClose,
  onSaved,
  accessoryId,
}: SettleCylinderDebtModalProps) {
  return (
    <Modal transparent visible={visible} animationType="fade" onRequestClose={onClose}>
      <View style={styles.overlay}>
        <KeyboardAvoidingView
          behavior={Platform.OS === "ios" ? "padding" : undefined}
          keyboardVerticalOffset={Platform.OS === "ios" ? 100 : 0}
        >
          <SettleCylinderDebtForm
            visible={visible}
            onClose={onClose}
            onSaved={onSaved}
            accessoryId={accessoryId}
          />
        </KeyboardAvoidingView>
      </View>
    </Modal>
  );
}

def _time_of_day(value: datetime) -> str:
  return "morning" if value.hour < 12 else "evening"

index.tsx

  const handlePriceInputChange = (
    gas: GasType,
    type: CustomerType,
    field: "selling" | "buying",
    value: string
  ) => {
    const comboKey = ${gas}:${type};
    setPriceInputs((prev) => {
      const nextValue = {
        selling: field === "selling" ? value : prev[gas]?.[type]?.selling ?? "",
        buying: field === "buying" ? value : prev[gas]?.[type]?.buying ?? "",
      };
      const next: PriceInputs = {
        ...prev,
        [gas]: {
          ...prev[gas],
          [type]: nextValue,
        },
      };
      const baseline = lastSavedPrices[gas]?.[type] ?? { selling: "", buying: "" };
      const matchesBaseline =
        (nextValue.selling || "") === (baseline.selling || "") &&
        (nextValue.buying || "") === (baseline.buying || "");
      if (matchesBaseline) {
        dirtyPriceCombosRef.current.delete(comboKey);
      } else {
        dirtyPriceCombosRef.current.add(comboKey);
      }
      return next;
    });
  };
  const handlePriceInputChange = (
    gas: GasType,
    field: "selling" | "buying",
    value: string
  ) => {
    const comboKey = gas;

      const nextValue = {
        selling: field === "selling" ? value : prev[gas]?.selling ?? "",
        buying: field === "buying" ? value : prev[gas]?.buying ?? "",
      };
      const next: PriceInputs = {
        ...prev,
        [gas]: nextValue,
      };
      const baseline = lastSavedPrices[gas] ?? { selling: "", buying: "" };
      const matchesBaseline =
        (nextValue.selling || "") === (baseline.selling || "") &&
        (nextValue.buying || "") === (baseline.buying || "");
      if (matchesBaseline) {
        dirtyPriceCombosRef.current.delete(comboKey);

        dirtyPriceCombosRef.current.add(comboKey);

  const handleSaveAllPrices = async () => {
    const dirtyCombos = Array.from(dirtyPriceCombosRef.current);
    if (dirtyCombos.length === 0) {
      Alert.alert("Nothing to save", "No price changes to save.");
      return;
    }
    setSavingPrices(true);
    try {
      for (const comboKey of dirtyCombos) {
        const [gas, type] = comboKey.split(":") as [GasType, CustomerType];
        const { selling, buying } = priceInputs[gas][type];
        const savedPrice = await savePrice.mutateAsync({
          gas_type: gas,
          customer_type: type,
          selling_price: Number(selling) || 0,
          buying_price: buying ? Number(buying) : undefined,
        });
        dirtyPriceCombosRef.current.delete(comboKey);
        const normalized = {
          selling: savedPrice.selling_price.toString(),
          buying: savedPrice.buying_price?.toString() ?? "",
        };

          ...prev,
          [gas]: {
            ...prev[gas],
            [type]: normalized,
          },

          ...prev,
          [gas]: {
            ...prev[gas],
            [type]: normalized,
          },
        }));
      }
      setPriceModalOpen(false);
    } finally {
      setSavingPrices(false);

        const { selling, buying } = priceInputs[gas];
        const savedPrice = await savePrice.mutateAsync({
          gas_type: gas,
          selling_price: Number(selling) || 0,
          buying_price: buying ? Number(buying) : undefined,
        });

          ...prev,

def _sum_company_cyl_before_day(session: Session, day: date, gas_type: str) -> int:
  prev = day - timedelta(days=1)
  return _sum_company_cyl_at_day_end(session, prev, gas_type)

  id: str

Created
company.py
from datetime import datetime, timezone

from fastapi import APIRouter, Depends, HTTPException, status
from sqlmodel import Session, select

from app.db import get_session
from app.models import CompanyTransaction
from app.schemas import CompanyCylinderSettleCreate, CompanyCylinderSettleOut
from app.services.posting import derive_day, normalize_happened_at, post_company_transaction

router = APIRouter(prefix="/company", tags=["company"])


@router.post("/cylinders/settle", response_model=CompanyCylinderSettleOut, status_code=status.HTTP_201_CREATED)
def settle_company_cylinders(
  payload: CompanyCylinderSettleCreate, session: Session = Depends(get_session)
) -> CompanyCylinderSettleOut:
  if payload.quantity <= 0:
    raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail="quantity_must_be_positive")

  if payload.request_id:
    existing = session.exec(
      select(CompanyTransaction).where(CompanyTransaction.request_id == payload.request_id)
    ).first()
    if existing:
      if payload.gas_type == "12kg":
        quantity = existing.buy12 or existing.return12
        direction = "receive_full" if existing.buy12 else "return_empty"
      else:
        quantity = existing.buy48 or existing.return48
        direction = "receive_full" if existing.buy48 else "return_empty"
      return CompanyCylinderSettleOut(
        id=existing.id,
        happened_at=existing.happened_at,
        gas_type=payload.gas_type,
        quantity=quantity,
        direction=direction,  # type: ignore[arg-type]
        note=existing.note,
      )

  happened_at = normalize_happened_at(payload.happened_at)
  buy12 = return12 = buy48 = return48 = 0
  if payload.gas_type == "12kg":
    if payload.direction == "receive_full":
      buy12 = payload.quantity
    else:
      return12 = payload.quantity
  else:
    if payload.direction == "receive_full":
      buy48 = payload.quantity
    else:
      return48 = payload.quantity

  txn = CompanyTransaction(
    happened_at=happened_at,
    day=derive_day(happened_at),
    buy12=buy12,
    return12=return12,
    buy48=buy48,
    return48=return48,
    total=0,
    paid=0,
    note=payload.note,
    request_id=payload.request_id,
    is_reversed=False,
  )
  session.add(txn)
  post_company_transaction(session, txn)
  session.commit()
  session.refresh(txn)

  return CompanyCylinderSettleOut(
    id=txn.id,
    happened_at=txn.happened_at,
    gas_type=payload.gas_type,
    quantity=payload.quantity,
    direction=payload.direction,
    note=txn.note,
  )

Nachgedacht für 56s
No — it’s very unlikely the welcome/setup page is “lost forever”. In practice one of these is happening:

1) The welcome page still exists, but routing no longer points to it
With expo-router, the first screen you see is driven by app/index.tsx and the various *_layout.tsx files. During the “Activities → Home” refactor, it’s common to accidentally remove/override the conditional redirect that used to send you to setup.

What to check (fast):

Do you have app/index.tsx?

Does it redirect to tabs unconditionally?

Is there a (setup) or (onboarding) folder that’s no longer referenced?

Quick search:

rg -n "welcome|setup|initialize|is_setup_completed|system/settings|/system/initialize" app src
Typical fix pattern (root redirect):

// app/index.tsx
import { Redirect } from "expo-router";
import { useSystemSettings } from "@/hooks/useSystemSettings"; // or wherever it lives

export default function Index() {
  const { data, isLoading } = useSystemSettings();

  if (isLoading) return null; // or a splash

  if (!data?.is_setup_completed) {
    return <Redirect href="/setup" />; // e.g. app/setup.tsx or app/(setup)/index.tsx
  }

  return <Redirect href="/(tabs)" />;
}
2) Setup is being skipped because the backend (or local app storage) still says “setup completed”
Even if you “started clean”, you may still have:

a Postgres volume with system_settings.is_setup_completed = true, or

a SQLite file still present, or

persisted AsyncStorage in the app.

Backend check:

If you’re using Postgres via docker compose, a “clean” restart often needs volume removal:

docker compose down -v
docker compose up -d
alembic upgrade head
Mobile check (common gotcha):

Uninstall the app / clear storage (Android) so it stops reusing old flags.

3) The welcome page file was deleted, but it’s still recoverable
Even without a commit, it can usually be recovered via:

VS Code Timeline (right-click folder/file → Open Timeline)

JetBrains Local History

Recycle Bin (Windows)

If it was committed at least once in the past:

git log -- app/path/to/welcome.tsx
git restore --source=<that_commit_sha> -- app/path/to/welcome.tsx
Immediate safety move (so nothing gets “lost” from here)
Before doing anything else, snapshot your current state:

git add -A
git commit -m "WIP: snapshot before continuing refactor"
If you don’t want to commit messy code, at least:

git diff > wip.patch
One important note
My “Memory” feature is currently disabled on your side; if you enable it (Settings → Personalization → Memory), I can keep track of the exact file paths/names we identify for your welcome/setup flow across sessions. But you don’t need that to fix this now.

If you paste your app/ tree (just the folder names) and the contents of app/index.tsx + app/_layout.tsx (or whatever exists), I’ll tell you exactly where the welcome screen should be wired back in and what redirect you’re missing.

ChatGPT:
rg is ripgrep. On your Windows PowerShell it’s simply not installed / not on PATH — nothing scary happened to the repo.

Option A (fastest): use built-in PowerShell search
From repo root:

$pattern = 'welcome|setup|initialize|is_setup_completed|system/settings|/system/initialize'
Get-ChildItem -Recurse -File app,src |
  Select-String -Pattern $pattern |
  Select-Object Path,LineNumber,Line
If you want it faster and less noisy (only TS/TSX):

$pattern = 'welcome|setup|initialize|is_setup_completed|system/settings|/system/initialize'
Get-ChildItem -Recurse -File app,src -Include *.ts,*.tsx |
  Select-String -Pattern $pattern |
  Select-Object Path,LineNumber,Line
Option B: install ripgrep (so you can use rg)
Windows (recommended):

winget install BurntSushi.ripgrep.MSVC
or Chocolatey (if you have it):

choco install ripgrep
Then reopen the terminal and rg will work.

What to do right after you run the search
Look specifically for:

app/index.tsx (or app/(tabs)/_layout.tsx) doing a redirect

any screen file named setup.tsx, welcome.tsx, (setup)/index.tsx, etc.

any logic reading /system/settings and checking is_setup_completed

The most common reason you “don’t see the welcome page anymore”
A root redirect got changed to always go to (tabs) (Home), instead of:

if !is_setup_completed → go to setup/welcome

else → go to tabs

So after you run the PowerShell search above, paste the lines it finds (especially anything in app/index.tsx and app/_layout.tsx), and I’ll tell you exactly what redirect needs to be restored.

One more “start clean” gotcha (not about code)
If you’re using Docker Postgres, you can still have an old volume where is_setup_completed=true.

To truly reset DB state:

docker compose down -v
docker compose up -d
alembic upgrade head
But do the code search first — most likely it’s routing.

ChatGPT:
Sure — here’s what each question is really asking, why it matters, and what the “safe default” answer usually is.

1) “Backend DB target right now: Postgres or SQLite?”
What I’m trying to learn
Which database you’re actually running while developing today.

Why it matters
Alembic migrations + constraints behave differently in SQLite vs Postgres.

Your refactor relies on:

UUID primary keys

UNIQUE constraints on nullable columns (request_id)

multi-column unique guards on ledger lines

timestamps/timezones (timestamptz)

These are much more reliable in Postgres.

What changes depending on your answer
If you’re on Postgres: we can implement the real schema exactly as intended.

If you’re on SQLite: we may need workarounds (less ideal) or run tests on Postgres anyway.

Safe default recommendation
Use Postgres for local dev + tests (docker-compose). SQLite only for very lightweight unit tests.

2) “Alembic migration: drop legacy tables or leave them?”
What I’m trying to learn
When you run the migration on your dev DB, do you want to delete the old tables (orders, collections, summaries, activities, etc.), or keep them around temporarily.

Why it matters
You said “start clean: no history migration/backfill.”
That typically implies you can drop old tables — but there’s one risk:

If some endpoints/UI still read old tables, dropping them will break the app immediately.

Two valid strategies
A) Leave legacy tables (safer during transition)

Create v2 tables and run the app.

Slowly migrate endpoints to v2.

Drop legacy tables only at the end.

B) Drop legacy tables now (cleaner but riskier)

Forces you to complete endpoint migration quickly.

Any leftover legacy code will crash immediately.

Safe default recommendation
Leave legacy tables for now, but treat them as “dead/unused” and remove later once v2 endpoints + tests are green.

3) “/cash/adjust posting: cash-only vs balancing account?”
What I’m trying to learn
When you manually adjust cash (like “I counted cash and it’s +50”), do you want the ledger to stay “double-entry-like” (every movement has a counterpart), or do you accept a “single-entry” style adjustment.

Why it matters
If you do cash-only, your ledger still works for balance reporting, but:

You can’t always explain why cash changed (other than note text).

Accounting-wise, it’s not balanced.

If you add a balancing account, you get audit clarity:

cash +50

adjustment_equity −50 (or vice versa)
So the ledger remains internally consistent.

Options
A) Cash-only (simplest)

One ledger line: cash += delta

Works fine for your app’s operational reporting.

B) Balanced with “cash_adjustments” / “equity” account (best audit)

Two lines:

cash += delta

cash_adjustments -= delta

Makes reports/audits cleaner.

Safe default recommendation
If you want minimal complexity now: cash-only.
If you care about audit trail / bookkeeping: add a balancing account (I recommend this).

Quick “answer guide” (what most people choose)
If you’re unsure, choose:

Postgres

Leave legacy tables for now

Balanced cash adjustments (cash + adjustment account)

If you reply with:

DB: Postgres or SQLite

Migration: drop legacy now or leave for later

Cash adjust: cash-only or balanced

Du:
the second question if i already git commit, we can always come back to the old code and return the legacy tables right? 
ChatGPT:
Yes — as long as the “old code” and its migrations are actually captured in Git, you can always go back. But there are two separate things to “go back” to:

Code state (Python/TS files)

Database state (tables/data in Postgres)

A git commit makes (1) easy. It does not automatically restore (2) unless your DB is recreated or you also revert migrations and apply them cleanly.

What Git commit guarantees
You can git checkout <old-commit> and get the legacy routes/services/models back exactly as they were.

You can re-run the app code from that commit.

What it does not guarantee by itself
Your current database might already have:

dropped legacy tables

created new v2 tables

advanced Alembic revision history

Switching code back doesn’t magically rebuild the DB to match.

Practical “rollback” options
Option A (most reliable): Drop/recreate DB
If you don’t care about preserving current dev data (you said “start clean” anyway):

stop backend

docker compose down -v (or drop the database volume)

docker compose up

checkout old commit

run alembic upgrade head for that old commit
✅ This restores legacy tables because you rebuilt the DB from the old migration history.

Option B: Alembic downgrade
Only works if:

you wrote downgrade steps correctly (often people don’t)

migrations are linear and reversible

no manual DB changes
It’s doable but less foolproof.

Option C: Keep legacy tables during migration
This avoids the whole problem:

create v2 tables

migrate endpoints

only drop legacy tables at the end
This is the lowest-risk approach while refactoring.

So… can you “return legacy tables” later?
Yes, if either:

you recreate the DB from the legacy commit’s migrations (best), or

you have correct Alembic downgrades.

Given your “start clean” constraint, the safest path is:

Commit now

Prefer keeping legacy tables until v2 is fully working + tests green

Then drop legacy tables in a final migration, knowing you can still recreate the old DB from the older commit if needed.

If you tell me which DB you’re using right now (Postgres in docker-compose?), I’ll give you the exact rollback commands for your setup.

Nachgedacht für 1m 8s
When I asked about a “balancing adjustment/equity account”, I meant this:

Context: what a cash adjustment is in the ledger
Your ledger is just deltas per account. For /cash/adjust you’re recording a manual correction (e.g., “I counted the cash and I’m missing 50” or “I found +100 extra”).

There are two valid ways to represent that in the ledger:

Option A — Cash-only entry (simplest)
You write one ledger line:

cash +100 (unit=money)

That’s it.

Pros

Very simple.

Matches your “ledger is deltas” idea.

Cons

Looks like money appeared/disappeared “from nowhere”.

Harder to report “how much of today’s cash movement was manual corrections”.

Option B — Cash + balancing line (audit-friendly)
You write two ledger lines with opposite amounts:

cash +100

cash_adjustments (or equity_adjustments) -100

Both are money unit.

Pros

You can always explain corrections: cash changed because of an adjustment.

Reporting becomes clean: “total manual corrections” is just SUM(account=cash_adjustments).

Makes reversals cleaner too (reverse both lines).

Cons

Adds one extra account name (but no extra table necessarily).

Important note: this is not “double-entry accounting” in the strict sense across your whole system (because you have money and count units, and you’re not tracking revenue). It’s simply a way to keep manual corrections explicitly categorized.

What I recommend
Use Option B with a dedicated account like:

account="cash_adjustments" (unit=money)

…and keep your dashboards ignoring it unless needed. It’s the best tradeoff: still simple, but much more auditable.

About your decision to drop legacy tables
That’s fine, but just be aware of the consequence:

A Git commit lets you restore old code anytime.

If the migration drops legacy tables, restoring them later usually means recreating the DB (drop volume / fresh DB + run old migrations) unless you wrote full Alembic downgrades.

Given your “start clean” approach, that’s usually acceptable.

If you want, paste your current /cash/adjust intent design (do you already have a cash_adjustments table, or is it ledger-only?), and I’ll tell you exactly where to implement the two-line posting and how reversals should look.

✅ Checklist items Codex should complete
Schema

 Add cash_adjustments intent table (UUID id, request_id unique nullable, happened_at timestamptz, day date index, delta int, note, reversed_id, is_reversed).

 (If you already have a legacy/v2 cash adjustments table) either reuse it or migrate to this shape, but don’t break the API.

Posting rules

 Implement posting for cash adjustment in the central posting engine:

ledger line: account="cash", unit="money", amount=delta

source_type="cash_adjustment", source_id=<intent.id>

derive day from happened_at (Europe/Berlin rule)

 Idempotency: same request_id returns the existing record and does not double-post.

 Reversal-only: “delete/edit” creates a reversal intent with reversed_id and posts opposite ledger lines.

API

 Keep the existing route(s) working (/cash/adjust and any list endpoints your UI uses).

 Keep request/response contract unchanged so frontend continues to work.

Queries / reports integration

 Ensure cash totals/reports read from SUM(ledger_entries) and therefore automatically reflect cash adjustments.

 If you have report event timelines that show “cash before/after”, ensure cash adjustment events appear correctly.

Tests (pytest)

 Posting test: creating a cash adjustment writes exactly 1 cash ledger line with correct sign + metadata.

 Idempotency test: same request_id doesn’t create second intent row or ledger lines.

 Reversal test: reversing negates the original ledger effect.

Goal: implement Option B for /cash/adjust in the new Intent Tables + Unified Ledger architecture.

Requirements (must)

Start clean

No backfill/migration of legacy data.

Database migrations should create only the v2 schema (legacy tables can be dropped).

Cash adjustment posting rule = 2 ledger lines (Option B)
For a cash adjustment intent with delta D (money units / minor units as per money_decimals):

Ledger line A: account="cash", unit="money", amount=+D

Ledger line B: account="cash_adjustments", unit="money", amount=-D

Same happened_at, day, source_type, source_id

No customer_id, no gas_type, no state

Put the note on both lines (or at least on the intent + lines)

Intent table for cash adjustments
If a v2 intent table doesn’t already exist, create it (SQLModel + Alembic migration). Use UUID PKs.
Suggested columns (match project conventions):

id, request_id (unique, nullable), happened_at (timestamptz), day (date)

delta_cash (int), note (nullable)

reversed_id (uuid nullable), is_reversed (bool default false)

Central posting engine

Posting must happen through the central posting service (same pattern as other intents).

Ledger inserts must be in the same DB transaction as inserting the intent row.

Reversal-only

If the API supports delete/edit for cash adjustments, implement them as reversal-only:

create a new cash_adjustment intent row with reversed_id=<original>

post ledger lines that negate the original effect (i.e., -D on cash and +D on cash_adjustments)

mark the original intent is_reversed=true

Idempotency

Enforce unique request_id on cash adjustments.

If a POST comes with an already-used request_id, return the existing record and do not double-post ledger lines.

Ledger uniqueness guard
Ensure the ledger has a uniqueness constraint/index like:

(source_type, source_id, account, gas_type, state, unit) unique
so posting can’t duplicate lines.

Reports

Cash totals must still be derived from SUM(ledger_entries.amount) where account="cash".

cash_adjustments is a separate account; do not include it in cash balance calculations.

(Optional but nice) expose a “cash adjustments total” number in reports if there’s already an obvious place.

Tests (pytest)
Add/extend tests covering:

Posting: one cash adjustment produces exactly 2 ledger lines with correct signs.

Idempotency: same request_id doesn’t add more ledger lines.

Reversal: reversing an adjustment nets balances back to original (cash and cash_adjustments both return to prior totals).

Acceptance criteria

Backend starts with empty DB, migrations apply cleanly.

Calling /cash/adjust results in two ledger lines (cash + balancing cash_adjustments) and correct report cash totals.

Idempotency and reversal behavior is proven by tests (tests green).

models.py

class CashAdjustment(SQLModel, table=True):
  __tablename__ = "cash_adjustments"

  id: str = Field(default_factory=_uuid, primary_key=True, index=True)
  request_id: Optional[str] = Field(
    default=None,
    sa_column=sa.Column(sa.String, unique=True, nullable=True),
  )
  happened_at: datetime = Field(
    default_factory=_utcnow,
    sa_column=sa.Column(sa.DateTime(timezone=True), index=True),
  )
  day: date = Field(sa_column=sa.Column(sa.Date, index=True))
  delta_cash: int
  note: Optional[str] = Field(default=None, nullable=True)
  reversed_id: Optional[str] = Field(default=None, nullable=True, index=True)
  is_reversed: bool = Field(default=False, index=True)

posting.py
  CompanyTransaction,

ACCOUNT_EXPENSE = "expense"
ACCOUNT_CASH_ADJUST = "cash_adjustments"


def post_cash_adjustment(session: Session, adjustment: CashAdjustment) -> list[LedgerEntry]:
  lines = [
    LedgerLine(account=ACCOUNT_CASH, unit=UNIT_MONEY, amount=adjustment.delta_cash, note=adjustment.note),
    LedgerLine(account=ACCOUNT_CASH_ADJUST, unit=UNIT_MONEY, amount=-adjustment.delta_cash, note=adjustment.note),
  ]
  return _insert_ledger_entries(
    session,
    source_type="cash_adjust",
    source_id=adjustment.id,
    happened_at=adjustment.happened_at,
    day=adjustment.day,
    lines=lines,
  )

import app.db as app_db
from app.models import LedgerEntry

    create_resp = client.post("/cash/adjust", json={"date": date, "delta_cash": -200, "reason": "mistake"})

def _sum_account(session: Session, account: str) -> int:
    rows = session.exec(select(LedgerEntry).where(LedgerEntry.account == account)).all()
    return sum(row.amount for row in rows)


def test_cash_adjustment_correction_and_audit(client) -> None:
    date = "2026-01-02"
    create_resp = client.post(
        "/cash/adjust",
        json={"happened_at": f\"{date}T10:00:00\", "delta_cash": -200, "reason": "mistake"},
    )
    assert create_resp.status_code == 201

    day = client.get("/cash/day", params={"date": date})
    assert day.status_code == 200
    assert day.json()["cash_end"] == 800
    with Session(app_db.engine) as session:
        assert _sum_account(session, "cash") == -200
        assert _sum_account(session, "cash_adjustments") == 200


    day = client.get("/cash/day", params={"date": date})
    assert day.status_code == 200
    assert day.json()["cash_end"] == 980
    with Session(app_db.engine) as session:
        assert _sum_account(session, "cash") == -20
        assert _sum_account(session, "cash_adjustments") == 20



def test_inventory_adjustment_undo_and_audit(client) -> None:
    init_inventory(client, date="2025-01-01", full12=0, empty12=0, full48=0, empty48=0)

    adjust_resp = client.post(
        "/inventory/adjust",
        json={
            "date": "2025-01-02",
            "gas_type": "12kg",
            "delta_full": 10,
            "delta_empty": 0,
            "reason": "count",
        },
    )
    assert adjust_resp.status_code == 201

    day = client.get("/inventory/day", params={"date": "2025-01-02"})
    assert day.status_code == 200
    summary = next(row for row in day.json()["summaries"] if row["gas_type"] == "12kg")
    assert summary["day_end_full"] == 10

    adjustments = client.get("/inventory/adjustments", params={"date": "2025-01-02"})
    assert adjustments.status_code == 200
    item = adjustments.json()[0]
    adjust_id = item["id"]

    delete_resp = client.delete(f"/inventory/adjust/{adjust_id}")
    assert delete_resp.status_code == 204
    day = client.get("/inventory/day", params={"date": "2025-01-02"})
    assert day.status_code == 200
    summary = next(row for row in day.json()["summaries"] if row["gas_type"] == "12kg")
    assert summary["day_end_full"] == 0

    adjustments = client.get("/inventory/adjustments", params={"date": "2025-01-02", "include_deleted": True})
    assert adjustments.status_code == 200
    row = next(entry for entry in adjustments.json() if entry["id"] == adjust_id)
    assert row["is_deleted"] is True
    with Session(app_db.engine) as session:
        assert _sum_account(session, "cash") == 0
        assert _sum_account(session, "cash_adjustments") == 0

from conftest import init_inventory
    day = date(2025, 6, 1)

    import app.db as app_db
    from app.models import CashDelta
    from app.services.cash import recompute_cash_summaries
    first_at = datetime(2025, 6, 1, 9, 0, tzinfo=timezone.utc).isoformat()
    second_at = datetime(2025, 6, 1, 9, 5, tzinfo=timezone.utc).isoformat()

    with Session(app_db.engine) as session:
        session.add(
            CashDelta(
                id="cashd_a",
                effective_at=effective_at,
                source_type="cash_adjust",
                source_id=None,
                delta_cash=10,
                reason="first",
                created_at=created_at,
                created_by=None,
            )
        )
        session.add(
            CashDelta(
                id="cashd_b",
                effective_at=effective_at,
                source_type="cash_adjust",
                source_id=None,
                delta_cash=20,
                reason="second",
                created_at=created_at,
                created_by=None,
            )
        )
        session.commit()
        recompute_cash_summaries(session, day, day)
        session.commit()

    assert resp.status_code == 201
    resp = client.post("/cash/adjust", json={"happened_at": second_at, "delta_cash": 20, "reason": "second"})

test_manual_adjustments.py

from __future__ import annotations

from sqlmodel import Session, select

def _ledger_for_source(session: Session, source_id: str) -> list[LedgerEntry]:
    return session.exec(
        select(LedgerEntry).where(
            LedgerEntry.source_type == "cash_adjust",
            LedgerEntry.source_id == source_id,
        )
    ).all()


def test_cash_adjustment_correction_and_audit(client) -> None:
        "/cash/adjust",
        json={"happened_at": f\"{date}T10:00:00\", "delta_cash": -200, "reason": "mistake"},
        json={"happened_at": f"{date}T10:00:00", "delta_cash": -200, "reason": "mistake"},
    )
    with Session(app_db.engine) as session:
        entries = _ledger_for_source(session, cash_id)
        assert len(entries) == 2
        assert _sum_account(session, "cash") == -200
        assert _sum_account(session, "cash_adjustments") == 0


def test_cash_adjustment_idempotency(client) -> None:
    date = "2026-01-03"
    payload = {
        "happened_at": f"{date}T09:30:00",
        "delta_cash": 150,
        "reason": "idempotent",
        "request_id": "cash-adjust-req-1",
    }
    first = client.post("/cash/adjust", json=payload)
    assert first.status_code == 201
    cash_id = first.json()["id"]
    second = client.post("/cash/adjust", json=payload)
    assert second.status_code == 201
    assert second.json()["id"] == cash_id

    with Session(app_db.engine) as session:
        entries = _ledger_for_source(session, cash_id)
        assert len(entries) == 2
        assert _sum_account(session, "cash") == 150
        assert _sum_account(session, "cash_adjustments") == -150

ChatGPT:

Nachgedacht für 1m 27s
Good — Codex implemented most of Option B, but based on the diff you pasted there are a few blocking inconsistencies you should fix before moving on to the next refactor phase.

What we achieved with this task (Option B /cash/adjust)
Core design achieved:

Added a new v2 intent model: CashAdjustment (request_id idempotency, happened_at/day, delta_cash, reversed flags).

Added posting rule in the central posting service that produces two ledger lines:

cash gets +D

cash_adjustments gets -D

Updated /cash/adjust to create CashAdjustment instead of the old Expense-based hack (looks like that was the goal).

Started/extended pytest coverage for posting + idempotency.

That’s the right direction.

What still looks wrong / incomplete (based on your pasted edits)
1) cash.py still contains old Expense-based cash-adjust code
You still have remnants like:

_get_cash_adjust_category() using ExpenseCategory

mixed Expense vs CashAdjustment selects/orders

old fields like amount, paid_from, kind, category_id still appearing in places

Even if some of it is unreachable, it’s risky: it can break imports, logic paths, or future refactors.

✅ Fix: make cash.py purely CashAdjustment-based for list/create/update/delete. Remove the category helper entirely.

2) Your ledger uniqueness guard might not actually guard (NULL problem)
You asked for uniqueness on:

(source_type, source_id, account, gas_type, state, unit)

But in both Postgres and SQLite, UNIQUE constraints allow multiple rows where nullable columns are NULL. Since Option B uses no gas_type/state, those are NULL, meaning duplicates may still slip through.

✅ Fix options (pick one):

Best: expression unique index using COALESCE(gas_type,'') and COALESCE(state,'')

Or: store sentinel empty strings instead of NULL for “not applicable” fields (less clean but works)

This is important because it’s the “last line of defense” against double-posting.

3) Your cash-adjust test assertions are inconsistent
In the snippet you pasted, one test asserts:

cash == -200

cash_adjustments == 0

That’s not Option B. For D = -200, Option B implies:

cash: -200

cash_adjustments: +200

So at least one test expectation (or the posting) is wrong.

✅ Fix: align all tests to:

SUM(cash) == D

SUM(cash_adjustments) == -D

4) test_reports_v2_unit.py still smells like legacy (CashDelta, recompute_cash_summaries)
Your “start clean / no legacy backfill” requirement conflicts with keeping tests that insert legacy tables or call recompute functions.

0004_ledger_unique_coalesce.py
"""add coalesce-based unique index for ledger entries

Revision ID: 0004_ledger_unique_coalesce
Revises: 0003_cash_adjustments
Create Date: 2026-01-30
"""
from alembic import op

revision = "0004_ledger_unique_coalesce"
down_revision = "0003_cash_adjustments"
branch_labels = None
depends_on = None


def upgrade() -> None:
    # Ensure uniqueness even when gas_type/state are NULL by normalizing to empty strings.
    op.execute(
        """
        CREATE UNIQUE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS ux_ledger_source_account_coalesce
        ON ledger_entries (
          source_type,
          source_id,
          account,
          COALESCE(gas_type, ''),
          COALESCE(state, ''),
          unit
        )
        """
    )


def downgrade() -> None:
    op.execute("DROP INDEX IF EXISTS ux_ledger_source_account_coalesce")

Why pytest is failing right now
1) ModuleNotFoundError: No module named 'tests'

2) ImportError: cannot import name 'CashDailySummary' from 'app.models'
tests/backend/test_collection_snapshots.py imports legacy v1 models (CashDailySummary, CollectionEvent) that no longer exist in your v2-only refactor. That test must be rewritten to validate v2 behavior (via ledger_entries sums and/or v2 report endpoints), or temporarily skipped.

That alone should make from tests.conftest import ... work (assuming tests/conftest.py exists).

Alternative (also fine): stop importing tests.conftest and move shared helpers to a real module like tests/backend/helpers.py, but adding __init__.py is the fastest.

Your Alembic log shows the index was created as:

ON ledger_entries (source_id, account, COALESCE(gas_type,''), COALESCE(state,''), unit)
It’s missing source_type, which you explicitly wanted in the uniqueness guard.

It should be:

ON ledger_entries (
  source_type,
  source_id,
  account,
  COALESCE(gas_type, ''),
  COALESCE(state, ''),
  unit
)
Even if tests don’t hit it yet, this is worth fixing immediately because it’s part of idempotency safety.

0004_ledger_unique_coalesce.py
"""add coalesce-based unique index for ledger entries

Revision ID: 0004_ledger_unique_coalesce
Revises: 0003_cash_adjustments
Create Date: 2026-01-30
"""
from alembic import op

revision = "0004_ledger_unique_coalesce"
down_revision = "0003_cash_adjustments"
branch_labels = None
depends_on = None


def upgrade() -> None:
    # Ensure uniqueness even when gas_type/state are NULL by normalizing to empty strings.
    op.execute(
        """
        CREATE UNIQUE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS ux_ledger_source_account_coalesce
        ON ledger_entries (
          source_type,
          source_id,
          account,
          COALESCE(gas_type, ''),
          COALESCE(state, ''),
          unit
        )
        """
    )


def downgrade() -> None:
    op.execute("DROP INDEX IF EXISTS ux_ledger_source_account_coalesce")

backend/alembic/versions_v2/0005_fix_ledger_unique_index.py

"""fix ledger unique index to include source_type and be NULL-safe

Revision ID: 0005_fix_ledger_unique_index
Revises: 0004_ledger_unique_coalesce
Create Date: 2026-01-30
"""
from alembic import op

revision = "0005_fix_ledger_unique_index"
down_revision = "0004_ledger_unique_coalesce"
branch_labels = None
depends_on = None


def upgrade() -> None:
    op.execute("DROP INDEX IF EXISTS ux_ledger_source_account_coalesce")
    op.execute(
        """
        CREATE UNIQUE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS ux_ledger_source_account_coalesce
        ON ledger_entries (
          source_type,
          source_id,
          account,
          COALESCE(gas_type, ''),
          COALESCE(state, ''),
          unit
        )
        """
    )


def downgrade() -> None:
    op.execute("DROP INDEX IF EXISTS ux_ledger_source_account_coalesce")
SQLite supports expression indexes and COALESCE, so this is fine.

Du:
why are we doing this? 
ChatGPT:
Because right now you have two different architectures living in the repo:

v2: intent tables → central posting → ledger_entries → reports derived from ledger

v1 leftovers: tests (and sometimes code) that still assume old models/tables like CashDailySummary, CollectionEvent, CashDelta, ExpenseCategory/Expense-based cash adjustments

Your goal (“start clean, v2-only, Option B cash adjust”) means: the source of truth is the ledger. So we’re doing this to make the repo internally consistent and to make tests meaningful again.

Concretely, we’re doing it for 4 reasons
Your test suite is currently lying / broken

test_collection_snapshots.py imports models that no longer exist (CashDailySummary, CollectionEvent), so pytest can’t even collect tests.

That’s not a functional bug in your app; it’s a mismatch between the tests and the new architecture.

To prevent double-posting and silent data corruption

/cash/adjust must be idempotent (same request_id → no extra ledger lines).

The uniqueness guard is the last line of defense. If it’s wrong (especially with NULLs), you can end up with duplicates even if your code has a bug later.

NULL handling matters for ledger uniqueness

In SQL, NULL doesn’t compare equal in a normal unique constraint.

Your cash-adjust ledger lines intentionally have gas_type = NULL and state = NULL.

Without the COALESCE-based index, you can post the same line twice and the DB might not stop you (engine-dependent behavior).

To make reports reliable and future-proof

In v2, reports must be computed from ledger sums.

Any tests checking old “summary tables” (CashDelta, CashDailySummary, etc.) will keep breaking as you remove v1 remnants.

What you get if we don’t do this
pytest keeps failing during collection → you lose your safety net

hidden duplication risk in the ledger → balances become untrustworthy

every refactor gets slower because you’re constantly fighting old assumptions

What you get once we finish this cleanup
Green test suite that actually validates the v2 behavior you care about

/cash/adjust is clean and auditable:

intent row exists

exactly 2 ledger lines per intent

idempotency guaranteed

reversal guaranteed

ledger-based reports stay correct as you add more intent types

The shortest mental model
We are aligning:

code ✅

DB constraints ✅

tests ✅
around one source of truth: ledger_entries.

That’s why.

If you want, paste what you mean by “why” (e.g., “why rewrite tests”, “why COALESCE index”, “why skip snapshot test”) and I’ll answer that specific angle with examples from your repo output.
